# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

- Test coverage is strongest around the risky rules code, especially [combatEncounterCasting.test.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/tests/combatEncounterCasting.test.ts). That lowers refactor risk if you keep future extractions behavior-preserving.

**My short recommendation**
1. Do `CS-HIST-01` first. It is isolated and low-risk.

- The player sheet side is cleaner. [PlayerCharacterPage.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/routes/PlayerCharacterPage.tsx), [usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/hooks/usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts), and [characterSheetMutations.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/mutations/characterSheetMutations.ts) form a more coherent route -> hook -> mutation pipeline.

**What This Means**
- `CS-HIST-01` is a UI gap, not a data-model problem. [CharacterHistorySection.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/components/player-character/CharacterHistorySection.tsx) is currently thin, while [characterTemplate.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/config/characterTemplate.ts) already has a solid `GameHistoryIntelSnapshotEntry` shape.
- `PreparedCastRequest` in [combatEncounterView.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/types/combatEncounterView.ts) is effectively your encounter command object already. That is the right seam for a later controller/engine extraction.
- Test coverage is strongest around the risky rules code, especially [combatEncounterCasting.test.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/tests/combatEncounterCasting.test.ts). That lowers refactor risk if you keep future extractions behavior-preserving.

**My short recommendation**
1. Do `CS-HIST-01` first. It is isolated and low-risk.
2. If you refactor next, target encounter execution only, not the whole app.
3. Extract pure encounter reducers/services out of [CombatEncounterPage.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/routes/CombatEncounterPage.tsx) before touching power modeling or broader state architecture.

### 30. User

things we used for combat mechanics should be in classes (at least that is my thought and that's what we will discuss).

1. a class for inflicting damage. this could be either a physical attack or a spell attack, but regardless, a damage output from the source --> damage inflicted (deducted) from the target. heal might be a subclass to this and working the other direction. maybe mana restoration
2. aura spells class
3. permanant passives (like increased alertness, social skills etc.) class
4. i cannot decide on spells like: summons, resurrection, control target, awareness, cure
5. maybe we should have a utility spell class, and we should put all that we cannot decide the action mechanic (or do not want to due to its intricacies)  
6. buffs (like stats and skills)

what is your opinion on this? let's discuss?

### 31. Assistant

Yes, but I would structure it a bit differently.

- I would **not** center the model on “spell classes” first.
- I would center it on **Action classes** and **Effect classes**.

My opinion on your list:

1. Damage class: yes, but make `DamageEffect`, `HealEffect`, and `ManaRestoreEffect` **siblings**, not `Heal` as a subclass of damage.
2. Aura class: yes.
3. Permanent passives: yes, but better as `PassiveEffect` or `PassiveModifierSource`, not a heavy spell class.
4. Summon / resurrection / control / awareness / cure: these are better as **action/ability handlers**, not one generic bucket.
5. “Utility spell” class: only as a temporary fallback. If it grows, it becomes a junk drawer fast.
6. Buffs: yes, `BuffEffect` / `ModifierEffect` is a good fit.

What I’d recommend:

- `Action`
  - `PhysicalAttackAction`
  - `DirectCastAction`
  - `AuraAction`
  - `SummonAction`
  - `ControlAction`
  - `KnowledgeAction`
  - `RestorationAction`

- `Effect`
  - `DamageEffect`
  - `HealingEffect`
  - `ManaEffect`
  - `BuffEffect`
  - `StatusEffect`
  - `AuraEffect`
  - `SummonEffect`
  - `HistoryEffect`

So:
- `PreparedCastRequest` becomes the transition seam.
- Actions decide **what happens**.
- Effects apply **how state changes**.

Short version: moving closer to OOP makes sense, but I’d avoid deep inheritance and use **small classes around actions/effects**, not “one class per spell type” first.

If you want, next I can give you a **very short mapping** of your current powers into these categories.

### 33. User

"""I would not center the model on “spell classes” first. 
I would center it on Action classes and Effect classes. """ explain this a little bit more.

### 34. Assistant

A spell is usually just a **source of behavior**, not the behavior itself.

Example:
- `Healing` can heal HP
- remove status
- add temp HP
- write history
- affect multiple targets

If you make one big `HealingSpell` class, it starts owning too many unrelated mechanics.

What I mean instead:

- `Action class` = decides intent
  - who is acting
  - what power/attack is being used
  - who the targets are
  - what effects should be produced

- `Effect class` = applies one kind of result
  - damage target
  - heal target
  - add buff
  - add status
  - spawn summon
  - write history entry

So:

- `Necrotic Touch` is an `Action`
- it may produce:
  - `DamageEffect`
  - maybe `HealingEffect`
  - maybe `LogEffect`

That is cleaner than stuffing everything into one spell class.

In short:
- `Action` = “what is being attempted”
- `Effect` = “what changes in state”

### 36. User

"Permanent passives: yes, but better as PassiveEffect or PassiveModifierSource, not a heavy spell class. " what do you mean by 'heavy spell class'?

### 37. Assistant

I mean a class that tries to own too much by itself.

For example, a “heavy spell class” might contain:
- targeting rules
- mana cost
- passive bonuses
- active cast logic
- aura logic
- status application
- UI labels
- history/log text
- validation rules

That becomes bloated fast.

For permanent passives like alertness/social bonuses, you usually do not need a full “spell object that acts.”
You just need something lighter, like:

- `PassiveModifierSource`
  - “while this power is unlocked, add +X to these stats/skills”

So “heavy spell class” = one large all-purpose class per power.
I think that would make this codebase harder to maintain.

### 40. Assistant

I mean logic units that handle **using** an ability, without forcing everything into one giant spell class.

For example:

- `SummonActionHandler`
  - validate summon choice
  - check mana
  - create summon result
  - return effects/state changes

- `ResurrectionActionHandler`
  - validate target
  - restore HP
  - remove death tags
  - return effects/state changes

- `AwarenessActionHandler`
  - validate CR cap
  - build intel snapshot
  - write history entry

So:

- `spell class` idea = “this power is an object with everything inside it”
- `action/ability handler` idea = “this module/class handles execution of this ability use”

It is a more focused responsibility.

### 46. Assistant

Yes, that is what I mean.

You would have a base effect type, then specialized effect types under it.

For example:

- `Effect`
  - `DamageEffect`
  - `HealingEffect`
  - `BuffEffect`
  - `StatusEffect`
  - `SummonEffect`
  - `HistoryEffect`
  - `ManaEffect`

So those items are the concrete effect classes.

Two valid designs:

1. OOP style
- base class: `Effect`
- subclasses: `DamageEffect`, `HealingEffect`, etc.

2. Lighter approach
- `type Effect = DamageEffect | HealingEffect | BuffEffect | ...`
- each effect is a typed object, not a class

For this codebase, I would lean toward:
- action handlers/classes
- typed effect objects or very light effect classes

So: yes, those would be the specialized effect types under the general effect concept.

### 49. Assistant

Fair. In this context, `handler` just means:

- a piece of code responsible for one job

Nothing more special than that.

Example:
- `ResurrectionHandler`
means:
- code whose job is to execute the `Resurrection` spell

It can be:
- a function
- a module
- a class

So when I say:

- `AwarenessActionHandler`
- `SummonActionHandler`

I simply mean:

- code responsible for executing that spell/action

If you dislike the word, we can stop using it and say instead:

- `executor`
- `resolver`
- `action class`
- `spell class`

`resolver` may be clearer than `handler` for this project.

### 51. User

i do not know what type (or typed) effect object is. i know what a class is, i know objects are instances of a class, but never heard of type effect object, hence i do not know how it differs from a class

### 52. Assistant

Good distinction.

What I meant is:

## Class version
You define a class, then create instances from it.

Example:
```ts
class DamageEffect {
  constructor(
    public targetId: string,
    public amount: number
  ) {}

  apply() {
    // do damage
  }
}
```

Then:
```ts
const effect = new DamageEffect("target-1", 12);
```

## Typed object version
No class at all. Just a plain object with a known shape.

Example:
```ts
type DamageEffect = {
  kind: "damage";
  targetId: string;
  amount: number;
};
```

Then:
```ts
const effect: DamageEffect = {
  kind: "damage",
  targetId: "target-1",
  amount: 12,
};
```

## Difference
- class = behavior + structure bundled together
- typed object = just structured data

So when I said “typed effect object,” I meant:
- a plain object
- checked by TypeScript
- not an instance of a class

In your codebase, `PreparedCastRequest` already works much more like the second style.

### 54. User

what's a module? that is new to me too

### 55. Assistant

A module is just:

- a file that contains code
- and exports things for other files to use

For example:

```ts
// damage.ts
export function applyDamage() {}
```

That file is a module.

So when I say:
- “put summon logic in its own module”

I mean:
- put it in its own file, like `summon.ts` or `summonResolver.ts`

Very simply:
- class = a blueprint for objects
- object = an instance / data value
- module = a file of related code

- module = a file of related code

### 60. User

i suppose this typed object is a language (code) related term, right? i do not know this code language we use for this project. i know python. does this exist in python?

### 61. Assistant

Yes. “typed object” is mostly a TypeScript-style idea.

Since this project uses TypeScript:
- objects can have explicit shapes enforced by the language

Example in TypeScript:
```ts
type DamageEffect = {
  kind: "damage";
  amount: number;
};
```

Python has similar ideas, but less central in normal usage.

Closest Python equivalents are:
- `dict` with expected keys
- `TypedDict`
- `dataclass`

Examples:

```py
effect = {"kind": "damage", "amount": 12}
```

or

```py
from typing import TypedDict

class DamageEffect(TypedDict):
    kind: str
    amount: int
```

or

```py
from dataclasses import dataclass

@dataclass
class DamageEffect:
    kind: str
    amount: int
```

So yes, the idea exists in Python, but TypeScript uses it more heavily and more naturally for plain structured objects.

### 63. User

ok, in general i suppose, i liked your action vs effect approach. so """Short version: moving closer to OOP makes sense, but I’d avoid deep inheritance and use small classes around actions/effects, not “one class per spell type” first.

If you want, next I can give you a very short mapping of your current powers into these categories.

 """
yes, give that

### 64. Assistant

Very short mapping:

- `Awareness`: mostly `PassiveEffect`; `Assess Character` = `KnowledgeAction` -> `HistoryEffect`
- `Body Reinforcement`: stat boost spell = `BuffAction` -> `BuffEffect`; revive spell = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` or `ResourceEffect`
- `Crowd Control`: control spell = `ControlAction` -> `StatusEffect` + ongoing control state
- `Elementalist`: attack spells = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect`
- `Healing`: `Heal`, `Wound Mend`, `Cure` = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` + `StatusRemovalEffect` + sometimes `TempHpEffect`
- `Light Support`: `Light Aura` = `AuraAction` -> `AuraEffect` + buff/debuff effects; mana restore spell = `RestorationAction` -> `ManaEffect`; passive bonuses = `PassiveEffect`
- `Necromancy`: `Summon Undead` = `SummonAction` -> `SummonEffect`; `Necrotic Touch` = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect` or `HealingEffect`; `Resurrection` = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` + `StatusRemovalEffect`
- `Shadow Control`: `Cloak of Shadow` = `AuraAction` -> `AuraEffect`; `Shadow Walk` = `UtilityAction`; `Shadow Manipulation` = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect`; `Shadow Soldier` = `SummonAction` -> `SummonEffect`

My short takeaway:
- powers are trees
- spells map to `Action` types
- actions produce one or more `Effect` types

That is the model I’d use.

### 65. Assistant

Very short mapping:

- `Awareness`: mostly `PassiveEffect`; `Assess Character` = `KnowledgeAction` -> `HistoryEffect`
- `Body Reinforcement`: stat boost spell = `BuffAction` -> `BuffEffect`; revive spell = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` or `ResourceEffect`
- `Crowd Control`: control spell = `ControlAction` -> `StatusEffect` + ongoing control state
- `Elementalist`: attack spells = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect`
- `Healing`: `Heal`, `Wound Mend`, `Cure` = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` + `StatusRemovalEffect` + sometimes `TempHpEffect`
- `Light Support`: `Light Aura` = `AuraAction` -> `AuraEffect` + buff/debuff effects; mana restore spell = `RestorationAction` -> `ManaEffect`; passive bonuses = `PassiveEffect`
- `Necromancy`: `Summon Undead` = `SummonAction` -> `SummonEffect`; `Necrotic Touch` = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect` or `HealingEffect`; `Resurrection` = `RestorationAction` -> `HealingEffect` + `StatusRemovalEffect`
- `Shadow Control`: `Cloak of Shadow` = `AuraAction` -> `AuraEffect`; `Shadow Walk` = `UtilityAction`; `Shadow Manipulation` = `AttackAction` -> `DamageEffect`; `Shadow Soldier` = `SummonAction` -> `SummonEffect`

My short takeaway:
- powers are trees
- spells map to `Action` types
- actions produce one or more `Effect` types

That is the model I’d use.

### 74. User

one note at this point. we currently have 8 (if i am not mistaken) powers. the number of powers will increase. i guess it will be around 20-25 towards the end. hence the number of spells will increase accordinly. take that into consideration as well and tell me what is a better solution for this project: classes/subclasses or your 'lighter refactoring' suggestion? i do not have an obsession for oop. it might be i am used to code in python and think coding in python, it is more simplistic in my mind; there are functions, classes, subclasses, and methods. decorators, handlers etc, does not mean much to me because all of them are part of these 'functions, classes, subclasses, and methods'. you are the typescript master. i am not even a novice in typescript. you now know where the direction of this project going, you know the language we use... decide, summarize your decision and why, and we can move on later.

### 75. Assistant

Decision: use the **lighter refactor**, not a big class/subclass tree for spells.

Why:
- with ~20-25 powers and many spells, “one class per spell” turns into class sprawl fast
- your current code already leans the other way, and [PreparedCastRequest](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/types/combatEncounterView.ts) is a good seam to build on
- most spells are just combinations of a few reusable results:
  - damage
  - healing
  - buffs
  - statuses
  - summons
  - history/log output
- TypeScript usually scales better here with **plain typed data + small resolvers/handlers**, not deep inheritance

So my recommendation is:
- keep **Action/Effect** as the conceptual model
- implement **spell resolvers/handlers per spell**
- keep **one central effect executor**
- use **very light classes only where they truly help**, not as the main architecture

In Python terms: closer to **dataclasses/dicts + functions** than a large subclass hierarchy.

If you want, next I can give you the **exact structure I would use** in this repo in 10-12 lines.

### 78. Assistant

Here is the exact structure I would use:

```ts
abstract class Action {
  abstract resolve(ctx: ActionContext): Effect[];
}

abstract class Effect {
  abstract apply(ctx: EffectContext): void;
}

class AttackSpellAction extends Action {}
class BuffSpellAction extends Action {}
class AuraSpellAction extends Action {}
class ControlSpellAction extends Action {}
class SummonSpellAction extends Action {}
class UtilitySpellAction extends Action {}
class KnowledgeSpellAction extends Action {}
class RestorationSpellAction extends Action {}

class DamageEffect extends Effect {}
class HealingEffect extends Effect {}
class ManaEffect extends Effect {}
class BuffEffect extends Effect {}
class StatusEffect extends Effect {}
class StatusRemovalEffect extends Effect {}
class SummonEffect extends Effect {}
class HistoryEffect extends Effect {}
class LogEffect extends Effect {}
```

My decision:
- use **light classes**
- not one heavy class per power
- not one huge inheritance tree
- spells resolve into reusable effects
- one spell can return multiple effects

So this keeps your Python-style class thinking, but avoids class explosion.

### 104. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
# Whole Power System Refactor Plan

## Summary
Refactor the current power/spell runtime into a light class-based Action/Effect architecture, while preserving current power/spell behavior, current local save compatibility, current UI flows, and `powers.json` as the metadata source. This refactor covers active spells, ongoing effects, aura behavior, summons, restoration, knowledge/history spells, and passive power-derived bonuses. `CS-HIST-01` is explicitly deferred until after this refactor.

## Architecture Changes
- Introduce a new runtime layer with these core contracts:
  - `ActionContext`
  - `EffectContext`
  - abstract `Action` with `resolve(ctx): Effect[]`
  - abstract `Effect` with `apply(ctx): void`
  - `EffectExecutor` that applies ordered effects to encounter/sheet state
- Use light action subclasses by spell category, then concrete spell classes under them:
  - category bases: `AttackSpellAction`, `BuffSpellAction`, `AuraSpellAction`, `ControlSpellAction`, `SummonSpellAction`, `RestorationSpellAction`, `KnowledgeSpellAction`, `UtilitySpellAction`
  - each current spell gets its own concrete class under the correct category
- Use reusable effect classes:
  - `DamageEffect`, `HealingEffect`, `ManaEffect`, `BuffEffect`, `StatusEffect`, `StatusRemovalEffect`, `AuraEffect`, `SummonEffect`, `HistoryEffect`, `LogEffect`
- Add one passive provider per power:
  - each power module exposes passive modifier/trait generation for derived runtime
  - `characterRuntime.ts` stops hardcoding power-specific passive branches and instead consumes provider output
- Keep `powers.json` and `powerData.ts` as the source of spell metadata:
  - mana cost
  - unlock level
  - targeting metadata
  - passive metadata
  - spell classes own execution logic, not metadata ownership
- Replace the current internal `PreparedCastRequest`-style spell assembly with an Action/Effect pipeline:
  - UI/request shapes stay stable at the route/component boundary
  - internal execution becomes `spell selection -> action instance -> effects -> executor`
  - `CombatEncounterPage.tsx` becomes orchestration only
- New runtime structure:
  - `src/powers/` for power registry, spell actions, and passive providers
  - `src/engine/` for effect execution and shared action/effect contexts
  - refactor existing logic out of `src/lib/combatEncounterCasting.ts`, `src/rules/powerEffects.ts`, and `src/config/characterRuntime.ts`

## Implementation Changes
- Build a power registry keyed by power id; each power module declares:
  - available spells
  - spell class factory/lookup
  - passive provider
- Migrate all current powers into the registry:
  - `Awareness`: `Assess Character`, artifact appraisal, alertness/inspiration passives
  - `Body Reinforcement`: stat buff spell, revive spell
  - `Crowd Control`: control spell, release spell, passive bonuses if any
  - `Elementalist`: direct damage spells/cantrip
  - `Healing`: `Heal`, `Cure`, `Wound Mend`
  - `Light Support`: `Light Aura`, mana restore, passive utility
  - `Necromancy`: `Summon Undead`, `Necrotic Touch`, `Resurrection`
  - `Shadow Control`: `Cloak of Shadow`, `Shadow Walk`, `Shadow Manipulation`, `Shadow Soldier`
- Preserve all current semantics:
  - same spell names and availability
  - same targeting rules
  - same mana usage and usage counters
  - same aura sharing/cleanup behavior
  - same undead/healing/necrotic behavior
  - same summon lifecycle
  - same game history/log side effects
- Keep the item model and item classes unchanged; only their integration points with passive/effect resolution move to the new engine
- Do the cutover as one branch-level rewrite:
  - build the new registry/actions/effects first
  - wire all current powers/spells/passives into it
  - switch the active routes/runtime to the new engine only after parity is reached
  - then remove obsolete switch/branch logic

## Test Plan
- Keep `npm run typecheck`, `npm test`, and `npm run build` green throughout the branch
- Add registry coverage:
  - every currently supported spell resolves to exactly one action class
  - every current power with passives exposes a passive provider
- Add parity tests for effect execution:
  - damage, healing, mana restore, buffs, status add/remove, summons, history/log output
- Preserve and keep passing the current combat regression suites, especially:
  - casting
  - special actions
  - encounter snapshot behavior
  - passive derived runtime behavior
- Add persistence compatibility tests:
  - existing saved character/item data hydrates without schema changes
  - existing active effects and usage state remain readable
- Acceptance criteria:
  - no UI flow changes required to use the system
  - no save reset required
  - no current power/spell behavior regression accepted

## Assumptions
- Strict backward compatibility is required for current local saved data and current gameplay behavior
- `CS-HIST-01` remains out of scope until after this refactor
- `B01` remains deferred
- The refactor changes internal architecture only; it does not redesign rules, rebalance powers, rename powers/spells, or change the item domain model
</proposed_plan>

### 179. Assistant

1. JSON  
In [powers.json](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/json_refs/powers.json), `Awareness` has:
- governing stat: `PER`
- passives: `Alerted Self`, `Awakened Insight`
- active spells/mechanics in data: `Assess Character`, `Artifact Appraisal`
- level scaling for `Assess Character`:
  - Lv1: stats + skills, `CR cap 6`
  - Lv2+: also powers + specials
  - Lv3+: techno-invisibility immunity
  - Lv5: share-results flag in data
- notes say `Assess Character` is bonus action, `0` mana, line of sight, instant

2. Spells under this power  
Currently in the codebase:
- passive behaviors:
  - `Alerted Self`
  - `Awakened Insight`
- spell exposed in the cast system:
  - `Assess Character`
- data-only, not implemented in the new runtime:
  - `Artifact Appraisal`

3. New action/effect implementation  
In [awareness.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/awareness.ts):
- `AwarenessPassiveProvider`
  - adds `alertness + awareness level`
  - adds `Techno-Invisibility Immunity` at level `>= 3`
- `AssessCharacterSpellAction extends KnowledgeSpellAction`
  - requires exactly one target
  - computes allowed CR as `min(PER + awareness level, cap-by-level)`
  - mana cost is `0`
  - returns:
    - `LogEffect`
    - `HistoryEffect`
- `HistoryEffect` writes a full intel snapshot into the caster’s `gameHistory`

Important gap:
- `Artifact Appraisal` is in JSON but has no action/effect implementation yet.
- `Awakened Insight` still lives in [characterTemplate.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/config/characterTemplate.ts), where normalization grants `+1 temporary inspiration` once when the power exists. It is not yet moved into the new passive provider layer.

If you want, next I can do the same short breakdown for `Body Reinforcement`.

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt

## Open tabs:
- T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt
- awareness.ts: src/powers/awareness.ts
- vite.config.ts: vite.config.ts
## My request for Codex:
i guess i am not understanding why do we need `KnowledgeSpellAction` ? it marks a spell as a “knowledge-type spell.”. why is this usefull to us, especially when it only does it for `assesscharacter` spellaction. so, why do we have both a parent and child class in here why not a single class?

can you please give at least 2-3 examples assuming that it will be usefull only if we extend it with adding more children in it. what sort of other children? i am struggling to follow the logic for that one

### 199. Assistant

Right now, by itself, `KnowledgeSpellAction` is not doing much. You are right to question it.

Why keep it:
- it gives us a category slot for future knowledge-type spells
- it lets us group similar spells before they diverge
- it avoids redesign later if `Awareness` grows

Examples of future children that would fit:
- `ArtifactAppraisalSpellAction`
  - inspect item quality, hidden bonuses, curse flags
- `AssessAreaSpellAction`
  - reveal traps, occult traces, hidden effects in an area
- `ReadAuraSpellAction`
  - inspect active buffs, curses, or magical signatures on a target

So the logic is:
- if `Assess Character` stays the only one forever, the parent is not very useful
- if we add more “reveal/inspect/intel” spells later, the parent becomes a clean category rather than dead weight

## My request for Codex:
All three examples that you provided could be examples for 'knowledge gathering' concept. but they will/can- not be a part of 'assess character' spell. we may have such examples, under awareness as new spells (and actually 'artifact appraisal' is one of them, yet they will be under awareness power as separate spells. so, evaluate this situation and tel me your opinoion

### 202. Assistant

My opinion: you are correct.

Those would be separate spells under the `Awareness` power, not sub-spells of `Assess Character`.
So the real hierarchy is:

- `Awareness` power
  - `Assess Character` spell
  - `Artifact Appraisal` spell
  - maybe other awareness spells later

Because of that, `KnowledgeSpellAction` only makes sense as a loose category base for multiple `Awareness` spells or even similar spells from other powers. If you want a simpler design, removing `KnowledgeSpellAction` and letting `AssessCharacterSpellAction` extend `Action` directly would be completely reasonable right now.

- `Awareness` power
  - `Assess Character` spell
  - `Artifact Appraisal` spell
  - maybe other awareness spells later

Because of that, `KnowledgeSpellAction` only makes sense as a loose category base for multiple `Awareness` spells or even similar spells from other powers. If you want a simpler design, removing `KnowledgeSpellAction` and letting `AssessCharacterSpellAction` extend `Action` directly would be completely reasonable right now.

### 205. Assistant

Yes, it can still be useful then, but only as a category base for multiple `Awareness` spells.

It becomes useful if those spells share knowledge-type behavior, for example:
- same style of target validation
- same “produce intel/history output instead of damage/buff” pattern
- same common helper methods

So:
- if `Assess Character`, `Artifact Appraisal`, and future `Awareness` spells stay mechanically similar, `KnowledgeSpellAction` is useful
- if they do not actually share logic, then it is just a label and not very useful

## My request for Codex:
about `historyeffect`. what i have in my mind is this:

===

cast: action
effect: effect in 'action/effect' mechanics. 
it's effect: i suppose it should be the parent `KnowledgeSpellAction`
knowledge type effects: that is currently not a part of the codebase at the moment but will be later. this effect should create a knowledge card.
card: a group of knowledge existing together. for instance, a section, or a few section or all of the sections of a character sheet is a card. OR, a section of an item info or full item info is a card. OR, a piece of story or the full story is a card.

===

when the spell is cast, it's effect should create a knowledge card. I assume this logic for all sorts of knowledge type effects. that card could be existing by itself and could be owned/posssessed by a character, could be updated/edited/copied (by the DM or the owning character), could be shared.  for that purpose, i brought up the concept of writing info to a character's history. but i am thinking from a broader perspective at the moment. thus, i want to ask you your opinion on this.

### 211. Assistant

I think your direction is stronger than `HistoryEffect`.

My opinion:
- `HistoryEffect` is too narrow
- a broader `KnowledgeEffect` that creates a `KnowledgeCard` is a better long-term model

Why:
- history is just one destination
- knowledge can be owned, stored, shared, edited, copied
- that fits `Assess Character`, `Artifact Appraisal`, lore/story reveals, documents, clues, DM handouts

So I would likely evolve this toward:
- `KnowledgeSpellAction`
  - produces `KnowledgeEffect`
- `KnowledgeEffect`
  - creates or updates a `KnowledgeCard`
- `KnowledgeCard`
  - character card
  - item card
  - story card
  - maybe encounter/intel card

Then:
- writing to character history becomes one way of surfacing a knowledge card, not the core model itself

So yes: I think your broader idea is better architecture than keeping everything as history entries.

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt

## Open tabs:
- T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt
- awareness.ts: src/powers/awareness.ts
- vite.config.ts: vite.config.ts

## My request for Codex:
regarding: "writing to character history becomes one way of surfacing a knowledge card, not the core model itself "

i am not sure if this how we should design this. i would like to hear your input on this as well. the idea with creating knowledgecard is make it "owned, stored, shared, edited, copied". in terms of owning, we need a mechanic and it should be a visual for players (real humans), considering that players will own knowledgecards and they will need to 'store them, read them, access them, share them, etc.'. so, the mechanics that we will be developing needs all options visually managable and controlled by the players through their character sheet. 

forget about the solution/application we currently have and proivde me your solution or alternatives.

### 214. Assistant

My preferred solution:

- do not make character history the main storage
- make `KnowledgeCard` its own real entity
- expose it in the character sheet as a dedicated `Knowledge` or `Intel` area

Why:
- history is a timeline
- knowledge is an inventory/library
- those are different jobs

Best structure:
- `KnowledgeCard`
  - id
  - type: character / item / story / location / faction / custom
  - title
  - sections
  - ownerCharacterIds
  - visibility / sharedWith
  - sourceSpell or sourceEvent
  - createdAt / updatedAt
  - tags
- character sheet:
  - `Knowledge` tab/section
  - list of owned cards
  - open/read card
  - copy/share card
  - maybe pin/favorite/archive

Good alternatives:
1. Separate knowledge library
- best long-term
- cleanest model
- supports ownership/sharing naturally

2. Character sheet subcollection
- each character stores owned knowledge cards directly
- simpler initially
- weaker if cards need cross-character sharing/copy lineage

3. History + extracted cards
- history logs the event
- separate cards hold the actual knowledge
- useful if you want both audit trail and reusable knowledge objects

My recommendation:
- use both
- `KnowledgeCard` is the real object
- history only logs that a card was discovered/updated/shared

That gives players a usable library, while still keeping an event trail.

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt

## Open tabs:
- T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt
- awareness.ts: src/powers/awareness.ts
- vite.config.ts: vite.config.ts

## My request for Codex:
i liked your suggestion, yet one caveat with it: knowledgecards will and should have versions, because card can be owned with many different characters and also a character can own many different version of the card, due to the fact that knowledge on these cards can change. assume that a knowledgecard is a characterknowledgecard (Ali's characterknowledgecard). another character (Veli) acquired it by using assesscharacter. later shared it with some another character (cemil) but before sharing it created a copy of it, altered it (Ali version 2) and shared it that way. OR, after acquiring it, the character that the cards points to (Ali) has evolved into something else in time (Ali version 3) and when the new updated card is owned by Veli a second time (it does not matter how), now Veli will have two characterknowledgecard: Ali version 1 (first card), Ali version 2 (altered version), and Ali version 3 (the evolved version).

evolving might be in many different ways, but we can assume (to make it simple) that it happens by gaining XP and spending that XP on the character.

considering this possibility, can you revise your suggestion, please?

### 217. Assistant

Yes. Then I would revise it like this:

- `KnowledgeCard` should be immutable per version
- edits or re-acquisitions create a new `KnowledgeCardVersion` or a new card revision, not overwrite the old one
- characters do not just “own a card”; they own references to specific versions/revisions

So the better model is:

- `KnowledgeEntity`
  - the subject, like `Ali`
- `KnowledgeRevision`
  - `Ali v1`
  - `Ali v2`
  - `Ali v3`
- `CharacterKnowledgeOwnership`
  - which character owns which revision(s)

Then:
- Veli can own `Ali v1`, `Ali v2`, `Ali v3`
- Cemil can own only `Ali v2`
- altered/copied cards become descendant revisions with lineage metadata like:
  - source revision
  - copied by
  - edited by
  - reason/source spell

My recommendation now:
- history logs events
- knowledge library stores revisioned cards
- character sheet shows owned revisions grouped by subject, not just one flat card

So conceptually:
- history = timeline
- knowledge entity = “who/what this is about”
- revision = one snapshot/version of that knowledge
- ownership = who currently possesses which versions

## My request for Codex:
sounds good. how would we carry this to the visuals for players? i suppose history would be a log as is now (you can correct me or suggest me alternatives at all times). what about player accessing the cards from their charactersheet?

### 220. Assistant

Yes, history should stay a log.

For visuals on the character sheet, I would do this:

- add a dedicated `Knowledge` section/tab
- inside it, group by subject/entity
  - `Ali`
  - `Ancient Sword`
  - `Temple of Ash`
- expanding a subject shows owned revisions
  - `v1`
  - `v2 (edited copy)`
  - `v3 (updated scan)`
- opening a revision shows the full card content

Player actions from the sheet:
- read
- rename local label
- duplicate
- share
- compare two revisions
- archive/hide
- mark trusted / altered / outdated

Best visual pattern:
- left column: knowledge subjects
- middle: revision list for selected subject
- right panel: selected card content

So the sheet becomes:
- `History` = what happened
- `Knowledge` = what you currently possess and can manage

```
Acquired character card Ali from Veli.
Drew two cards and ended turn.
Attacked opponent and reduced their health.
Cast assess character on Ali.
Played a defense card to block incoming damage.
```

both `Ali` could be a link to Ali's card for that specific version. The player might hover on it and it would be openning up hover-window showing the specific version of the card data, and/or the player might click on it and that would open a pop-up-window to that specific version of the card.

### 223. Assistant

I think that is a good solution.

Best version of it:
- `History` stays an event log
- history entries can link to exact knowledge revision ids
- `Knowledges` is the library/management area

So:
- in `History`, `Ali` links to the exact revision involved in that event
- hover = quick preview
- click = full card modal/popup
- `Knowledges` = browse all owned subjects and revisions

That is strong because:
- log preserves context of how/when a version was acquired
- library preserves long-term management
- both surfaces point to the same underlying revision object

So yes, I would support that design.

### 254. Assistant

`Body Reinforcement` in [powers.json](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/json_refs/powers.json):

- governing stat: `STAM`
- main spell scales by level:
  - Lv1: self target, `+1` to one of `STR/DEX/STAM`, mana `2`
  - Lv2: can target others by touch, still `+1`, mana `2`
  - Lv3: `+2`, mana `3`
  - Lv4: `+2` plus `DR +1`, mana `3`
  - Lv5: `+3` plus `DR +2`, mana `4`
- cantrip:
  - unlocked at Lv2
  - revive from incapacitated to `1 HP`, `1/day`
  - at Lv5 revive becomes `4 HP`

Spells under this power in the codebase:

- main buff spell: `Body Reinforcement`
- cantrip/special spell: `Body Reinforcement` revive
- no passive spell for this power; its passive provider is empty in [bodyReinforcement.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/bodyReinforcement.ts)

New action/effect implementation in [bodyReinforcement.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/bodyReinforcement.ts):

- `BodyReinforcementSpellAction extends BuffSpellAction`
- it builds the actual buff through `buildActivePowerEffect(...)`
- it requires one valid target and one selected physical stat
- it returns:
  - `BuffEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- the buff content itself is still coming from the shared power-effect builder, so level-based stat bonus and DR come from the existing rules

- `BodyReinforcementReviveSpellAction extends RestorationSpellAction`
- it checks eligibility through `getBodyReinforcementReviveState(...)`
- current encounter behavior is manual trigger only, not auto turn-advance
- it returns:
  - `ResourceEffect` to set HP to `1` or `4`
  - `UsageCounterEffect` to spend the daily revive use
  - `LogEffect`

Short takeaway:
- BR has one main buff spell plus one revive cantrip
- no passive provider logic
- buff path = `BuffSpellAction -> BuffEffect`
- revive path = `RestorationSpellAction -> ResourceEffect + UsageCounterEffect`

### 255. Assistant

`Body Reinforcement` in [powers.json](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/json_refs/powers.json):

  - Lv5: `+3` plus `DR +2`, mana `4`
- cantrip:
  - unlocked at Lv2
  - revive from incapacitated to `1 HP`, `1/day`
  - at Lv5 revive becomes `4 HP`

Spells under this power in the codebase:

- main buff spell: `Body Reinforcement`
- cantrip/special spell: `Body Reinforcement` revive
- no passive spell for this power; its passive provider is empty in [bodyReinforcement.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/bodyReinforcement.ts)

New action/effect implementation in [bodyReinforcement.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/bodyReinforcement.ts):

- `BodyReinforcementSpellAction extends BuffSpellAction`
- it builds the actual buff through `buildActivePowerEffect(...)`
- it requires one valid target and one selected physical stat
- it returns:
  - `BuffEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- the buff content itself is still coming from the shared power-effect builder, so level-based stat bonus and DR come from the existing rules

- `BodyReinforcementReviveSpellAction extends RestorationSpellAction`
- it checks eligibility through `getBodyReinforcementReviveState(...)`
- current encounter behavior is manual trigger only, not auto turn-advance
- it returns:
  - `ResourceEffect` to set HP to `1` or `4`
  - `UsageCounterEffect` to spend the daily revive use
  - `LogEffect`

Short takeaway:
- BR has one main buff spell plus one revive cantrip
- no passive provider logic
- buff path = `BuffSpellAction -> BuffEffect`
- revive path = `RestorationSpellAction -> ResourceEffect + UsageCounterEffect`

Answers:

1. BP action:
- `BoostPhysiqueSpellAction`
- yes, it is a child of `BuffSpellAction`
- `BuffSpellAction` is the parent/category class
- currently BP is the only implemented child under that parent

2. BP effect:
- in the Action/Effect model, BP produces a `BuffEffect`
- `buildActivePowerEffect(...)` is not the effect class; it is a shared helper that builds the active-effect payload
- that helper is also used by:
  - `Light Aura`
  - `Cloak of Shadow`

3. `RestorationSpellAction`:
- yes, parent class
- current children:
  - `BruteDefianceSpellAction`
  - `HealingSpellAction`
  - `ManaRestoreSpellAction`
  - `ResurrectionSpellAction`

4. `ResourceEffect`:
- child class of `Effect`, not a parent
- current users:
  - `BruteDefianceSpellAction`
  - `ResurrectionSpellAction`

5. `UsageCounterEffect`:
- child class of `Effect`, not a parent
- current users:
  - `BruteDefianceSpellAction`
  - `HealingSpellAction`
  - `ElementalistSpellAction`
  - `ManaRestoreSpellAction`

- `67d51a1` `Rename Body Reinforcement spells`

## My request for Codex:
2. I think there is a problem with this. Light Aura and Cloak of Shadow are two aura spells. they are activated yes, but they are not target oriented spells. aura spells benefits all allies, thus everybody in the same party get effected from aura spells, unless the aura owner specifically exclude a party member by identifying it not an ally. there will be more aura spells and more targetted spells joining to this mechanics. i just want to be sure if the method you chose is a good one. so, what do you think?

### 294. Assistant

I think your concern is valid.

`buildActivePowerEffect(...)` is currently doing two jobs:
- building targeted BP-style buff payloads
- building aura-source payloads for `Light Aura` and `Cloak of Shadow`

That works for now, but it is not the best long-term shape if more aura spells are coming.

My opinion:
- keep BP on `buildActivePowerEffect(...)` for now if it stays simple
- move aura spells toward their own helper, something like:
  - `buildAuraSourceEffect(...)`
  - or `buildAuraSpellEffect(...)`

Why:
- targeted buff logic and aura-source logic are not the same mechanic
- aura spells are party-scope relationship effects, not normal single-target buffs
- if more aura spells come, mixing both into one builder will get messy fast

So short answer:
- current method is acceptable temporarily
- long-term, aura spell construction should be separated from targeted buff construction

### 308. Assistant

`Crowd Control` has these spells in the codebase:

- `Control Target`
- `Release Target`
- passive/cantrip bonuses:
  - Lv2: `+1 social`, `+1 intimidation`
  - Lv5: also `+1 mechanics`, `+1 technology`

Action classes:

- parent: `ControlSpellAction`
- children:
  - `ControlTargetSpellAction`
  - `ReleaseControlSpellAction`

Effect classes used:

- `Control Target`
  - `StatusEffect`
  - `OngoingStateEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Release Target`
  - `StatusRemovalEffect`
  - `OngoingStateEffect`
  - `LogEffect`

Behavior under new mechanics:

- `ControlTargetSpellAction`
  - validates target type from level rules
  - pre-Lv5: living only
  - Lv5: can also affect allowed non-living targets, but not unsupported summons
  - checks max controlled target count
  - blocks targets with `crowd_control_immunity`
  - auto-resolves contest:
    - caster = `CHA + INT`
    - target = `WITS + CHA`
    - tie = failure
  - successful targets get:
    - `Paralyzed`
    - `Controlled by <caster>`
    - an ongoing `crowd_control` state with maintenance/break rules
  - logs success/failure per target
  - cast mana cost is `0`

- `ReleaseControlSpellAction`
  - removes:
    - `Paralyzed`
    - `Controlled by <caster>`
  - emits an ongoing-state release change so the maintained control state is removed
  - logs the release
  - mana cost is `0`

One important note:
- the spell action creates the ongoing control state
- upkeep spending, break-on-damage cleanup, and drop logic are still handled later in [CombatEncounterPage.tsx](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/routes/CombatEncounterPage.tsx), not fully inside the action class

Passive implementation:
- [crowdControl.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/crowdControl.ts) also has `CrowdControlPassiveProvider`
- it reads the cantrip mechanics and feeds those skill bonuses into the passive registry

### 331. Assistant

`Elementalist` spells in the codebase:

- `Elemental Bolt`
- `Elemental Cantrip`

Action classes:

- parent: `AttackSpellAction`
- child: `ElementalistSpellAction`
- one child class currently handles both `Elemental Bolt` and `Elemental Cantrip`

Effect classes used:

- `DamageEffect`
- `HealingEffect`
- `UsageCounterEffect`
- `LogEffect`

Behavior under the new mechanics:

- `ElementalistSpellAction`
  - validates the selected damage type
  - calls `buildDirectDamageCastResolution(...)`
  - turns the returned results into effects

- `Elemental Bolt`
  - main damaging spell
  - damage is built from `INT` plus level-based flat bonus
  - target count and split-damage rules scale by level
  - at low level, the chosen element gets locked until long rest
  - at higher levels, damage type becomes freely selectable
  - at level 5, `necrotic` becomes available and costs more mana than the other damage types
  - at higher levels, split damage can also be boosted by extra mana

- `Elemental Cantrip`
  - unlocked at level 2
  - costs `0` mana
  - uses the same action class
  - has its own level-based damage/target rules
  - level 5 can split to 2 targets
  - `necrotic` is explicitly disallowed for the cantrip

Special behavior:
- if `necrotic` is used on living targets, damage is increased by vulnerability rules
- if `necrotic` is used on undead targets, it heals instead of damaging, so the action emits `HealingEffect` instead of `DamageEffect`
- it can target transient summons in encounter flow

Short version:
- one spell-action class
- mostly `DamageEffect`
- sometimes `HealingEffect` for necrotic-on-undead
- `UsageCounterEffect` is only for the low-level locked-element rule

### 334. Assistant

Quite different overall.

- Biggest difference:
  - current model has `2` spells: `Elemental Bolt` and `Elemental Cantrip`
  - your model has `3` spells: `Elemental Bolt`, `Elemental Cantrip`, `Elemental Split`
  - in current code, split-style multi-target damage is folded into `Elemental Bolt`; there is no separate `Elemental Split`

- `Elemental Bolt`:
  - current matches the low-level lock, level 3 free element switching, and level 5 necrotic cost increase
  - but current `Elemental Bolt` becomes multi-target at higher levels
  - your version keeps `Elemental Bolt` as the direct spell and moves split behavior into `Elemental Split`

- `Elemental Cantrip`:
  - current is close at levels 2-4
  - current level 5 is `bonus action`, up to `2` targets
  - your version says level 5 should be `standard action`, up to `3` targets
  - current code also does not enforce the “cannot be cast if another attack happened earlier this turn” rule

- Architecture:
  - current runtime uses one action class, `ElementalistSpellAction`, for both spells
  - your version wants much cleaner spell separation, especially `Elemental Cantrip` and `Elemental Split` not inheriting from `Elemental Bolt`

Short version:
- current model is close on the core damage-type idea
- but it is materially different from your proposed spell structure and targeting rules
- the missing piece is mainly `Elemental Split` as its own spell

### 337. Assistant

1. `AttackSpellAction` children:
- `ElementalistSpellAction`
- `NecroticTouchSpellAction`
- `ShadowManipulationSpellAction`

2. `ElementalistSpellAction` children:
- none
- it is currently a concrete class, not a parent class

3. `UsageCounterEffect` in `Elementalist`:
- it is used to store the low-level locked damage type until long rest
- specifically, at low levels when the first element is chosen, it writes that selection into usage state
- it is not counting attacks here; it is storing the chosen element selection

4. On coding principles:
- yes, your newer suggestion is cleaner architecturally
- especially because `Elemental Bolt`, `Elemental Cantrip`, and `Elemental Split` become clearly separate spells with separate rules
- that usually improves maintainability and readability

Tradeoff:
- it is a bit more code
- but it is less mixed logic per spell

My opinion:
- if your design intent is stable, your split is better than the current merged `Elemental Bolt`/split approach
- cleaner spell separation is better here, not worse

- it is used to store the low-level locked damage type until long rest
- specifically, at low levels when the first element is chosen, it writes that selection into usage state
- it is not counting attacks here; it is storing the chosen element selection

4. On coding principles:

- that usually improves maintainability and readability

Tradeoff:
- it is a bit more code
- but it is less mixed logic per spell

My opinion:
- if your design intent is stable, your split is better than the current merged `Elemental Bolt`/split approach
- cleaner spell separation is better here, not worse

### 350. Assistant

### 351. Assistant

`Healing` spells in the codebase:

- `Heal`
- `Cure`
- `Wound Mend`

Action classes:

- parent: `RestorationSpellAction`
- child: `HealingSpellAction`
- one child class currently handles all 3 spells by branching on `selectedSpellId`

Effect classes used:

- `HealingEffect`
- `DamageEffect`
- `StatusRemovalEffect`
- `HistoryEffect`
- `UsageCounterEffect`
- `LogEffect`

Behavior under the new mechanics:

- `Heal`
  - normal healing spell
  - healing amount comes from `INT + level flat bonus`
  - can be allocated across multiple targets when allowed by level
  - removes `bleeding`
  - level 4+: can regrow limbs, which adds a history note
  - level 5: can overheal once per target per day into temporary HP, capped by `STAM`

- `Cure`
  - separate spell in current code
  - unlocked at level 3
  - mana cost `3`
  - removes `bleeding`, `poison`, `disease`, `curse`
  - current implementation treats it mainly as cleansing, not HP restoration

- `Wound Mend`
  - cantrip
  - unlocked at level 3
  - mana cost `0`
  - heals flat `2 / 3 / 4` by level 3/4/5
  - stops bleeding
  - limited to `2 uses per target per day`

Special behavior:
- if the target is undead, healing is reversed into `radiant` damage instead of healing
- that is why `HealingSpellAction` may emit either `HealingEffect` or `DamageEffect` depending on the target

Short version:
- one action class
- multiple effect classes
- `Heal` = healing/restoration
- `Cure` = cleanse
- `Wound Mend` = cantrip heal with per-target daily limit

# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.

</INSTRUCTIONS>

### 361. Assistant

Mostly close, but not identical.

- Spell naming differs:
  - current: `Heal`, `Cure`, `Wound Mend`
  - your version: `Heal Living`, `Holy Purge`, `Healing Touch`

- `Heal / Heal Living`:
  - current is very close
  - L1 touch, `INT+1`, mana `2`
  - L2 range, split across up to `4` targets
  - L4 limb regrowth
  - L5 overheal up to target `STAM`
  - main difference: current L3-L5 base spell still carries status-removal data in JSON, though `Cure` is handled separately in runtime

- `Cure / Holy Purge`:
  - current is similar in function, but not in cost
  - current `Cure` is unlocked at L3, touch at L3, ranged at L4+, which matches
  - but current mana cost is `3`, not `2`
  - current removes `poison`, `disease`, `curse`; `bleeding` is excluded in runtime for `Cure`

- `Wound Mend / Healing Touch`:
  - current is functionally very close
  - L3/L4/L5 heal `2 / 3 / 4`
  - that matches your `HL / 2 (round up)` values for `INT+3 / +4 / +5`
  - per-target `2/day` limit also matches

Coding-wise:
- your version is cleaner
- it separates the three spells more explicitly
- current code still has one `HealingSpellAction` branching internally for all three spells, so it is more mixed than your proposed model

### 374. Assistant

### 375. Assistant

`Light Support` currently has:

- active spells:
  - `Light Aura`
  - `Mana Restore`
- folded into `Light Aura`, not separate:
  - `Expose Darkness` at level `5`
- passive/cantrip:
  - `Nightvision`
  - mana bonus `+1 / +2 / +3`

Action classes:

- parent classes:
  - `AuraSpellAction`
  - `RestorationSpellAction`
- children:
  - `LightAuraSpellAction`
  - `ManaRestoreSpellAction`

Effect classes:

- `Light Aura`
  - `AuraEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Mana Restore`
  - `ManaEffect`
  - `UsageCounterEffect`
  - `LogEffect`

Behavior under current action/effect runtime:

- `LightAuraSpellAction`
  - builds the aura source through `buildActivePowerEffect(...)`
  - auto-applies the aura to:
    - caster
    - all valid allies in the same party
  - at level `5`, it also auto-applies enemy-side linked aura effects for `Expose Darkness`
  - those enemy linked effects reduce physical/elemental resistance by `1`
  - returns one `AuraEffect` containing:
    - source aura
    - ally linked aura effects
    - enemy linked expose-darkness effects
  - logs the cast

- `ManaRestoreSpellAction`
  - unlocked from level `4`
  - restores mana equal to `APP * 2`
  - costs `0` mana
  - limited to `1` use per long rest
  - uses `UsageCounterEffect` to spend that long-rest use
  - logs the restore

Passive/cantrip implementation:
- `LightSupportPassiveProvider`
  - adds `Nightvision`
  - adds the cantrip mana bonus through the passive registry
- so the cantrip is not an action class; it is passive runtime output

```6. Light Support (LS): (App)

6.1. Let There Be Light (LTBL) - Active (Aura): Create a light source on yourself. It provides vision in darkness. This power creates an aura effect that must be activated.
Level 1. Provides bonuses to Neutral/friendly/allied targets in range.
LTBL Bonus:+2 hit (+2d10), +1 DR.
Action: Standard
Mana Cost: 2
Range: 50m Radius
Duration: 30 Minutes

Level 2. Hostile targets cannot see your summoned light any more and cannot detect you because of it. Your light source bonus grows.
LTBL Bonus:+2 hit (+2d10), +1 DR
Action: Standard
Mana Cost: 2
Range: 50m Radius
Duration: 1 Hour

Level 3.
LTBL Bonus:+3 hit, +1 DR, +1 Soak
Action: Standard
Mana Cost: 2
Range: 50m Radius
Duration: 2 Hours

Level 4. Its range widens. Once per long rest, or once in each portal, 
LTBL Bonus:+3 hit, +2 DR, +1 Soak
Action: Standard
Mana Cost: 2
Range: 100m Radius
Duration: 4 Hours

Level 5.
LTBL Bonus:+4 hit, +2 DR, +2 Soak
Action: Standard
Mana Cost: 2
Range: 100m Radius
Duration: 8 Hours


6.2. Lunar Bless (LB) - Passive: Gain +1 mana bonus per level and provide night vision.
Duration: Passive

Level 1. Mana Bonus: +1
Night Vision: Self

Level 2. Mana Bonus: +2
Night Vision: Self + 1

Level 3. Mana Bonus: +3
Night Vision: Self + 3

Level 4. Mana Bonus: +4
Night Vision: Self + 3

Level 5. Mana Bonus: +5
Night Vision: Self + 4


6.3. Lessen Darkness (LD) - Active: Activates with the 5th Level of LTBL. Darkness-based and evil creatures in range of LTBL lose one Resistance Level (RL). If they are immune (RL2) to physical/elemental attacks, they become resistant (RL1) to those attacks; if they are resistant (RL1), they lose their resistance (RL0); if they do not have any resistance (RL0), they become vulnerable (RL-1): RL2 -> RL1, RL1 -> RL0, RL0 -> RL-1.

Level 1. Unavailable at this level

Level 2. Unavailable at this level

Level 3. Unavailable at this level

Level 4. Unavailable at this level

Level 5. Activated. Works with LTBL and acquires all other specifics from LTBL.
Constraint: This effect is active only while LTBL is active.


6.4. Luminous Restoration (LR) - Active: Restore lost mana of a friendly target (self included).

Level 1. Unavailable at this level

Level 2. Unavailable at this level

Level 3.

Action: Standard
Mana Cost: None
Range: 25m
Duration: Instant

Level 4.

Action: Standard
Mana Cost: None
Range: 25m
Duration: Instant

Level 5.

Action: Standard
Mana Cost: None
Range: 25m

```

### 378. Assistant

Quite different.

- Spell structure:
  - current has `Light Aura` + `Mana Restore`, with `Expose Darkness` folded into level 5 `Light Aura`
  - your version has `Let There Be Light`, `Lunar Bless`, `Lessen Darkness`, `Luminous Restoration` as cleaner separate concepts

- Aura numbers/duration:
  - current L1 is `+2 hit, +0 DR`, not `+1 DR`
  - current durations are `10m / 30m / 1h / 3h / 8h`, not `30m / 1h / 2h / 4h / 8h`
  - current L2 already has `+1 DR`

- Passive:
  - current passive is only `Nightvision` + mana bonus `+1 / +2 / +3` at levels `1 / 3 / 5`
  - your version is much stronger and scales every level to `+1..+5` mana, with staged night-vision sharing

- Darkness debuff:
  - current level 5 enemy effect only reduces resistance by `1`
  - your `Lessen Darkness` also pushes `RL0 -> RL-1` into vulnerability
  - current implementation does not go that far

- Mana restore:
  - current unlocks at level `4`, not `3`
  - current restore is `APP x 2` at levels `4-5`
  - your version is `APP` at L3, `APP x 2` at L4, `APP x 3` at L5

Coding-wise:
- your version is cleaner and more explicit
- current model is more compressed, with passive scaling and darkness debuff simplified
- if your new spec is the intended design, it should also become a TODO like the others

### 392. Assistant

`Necromancy` currently has:

- spells:
  - `Summon Undead`
  - `Necrotic Touch`
  - `Resurrection`
  - current extra runtime action: `Dismiss Summon`
- passive/cantrip:
  - melee bonus
  - hostile-undead aggro reduction

Action classes:

- parent classes:
  - `SummonSpellAction`
  - `AttackSpellAction`
  - `RestorationSpellAction`
- children:
  - `SummonUndeadSpellAction`
  - `NecroticTouchSpellAction`
  - `ResurrectionSpellAction`

Effect classes:

- `Summon Undead`
  - `SummonEffect`
  - sometimes `AuraEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Necrotic Touch`
  - `DamageEffect`
  - `HealingEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Resurrection`
  - `ResourceEffect`
  - `StatusRemovalEffect`
  - `LogEffect`

Behavior under current action/effect runtime:

- `Summon Undead`
  - builds summon choice from summon rules
  - can spawn skeleton / skeleton king / zombie depending on level
  - dismisses replaced summons when needed
  - inherits caster aura effects onto summons when relevant
  - `Dismiss Summon` is handled inside the same action class

- `Necrotic Touch`
  - requires resolved attack outcome first
  - on miss: only logs, still spends mana
  - on hit: deals necrotic damage
  - always heals the caster by `Necromancy` level
  - heals undead targets instead of damaging them
  - blocked by shadow/incorporeal-type targets

- `Resurrection`
  - sets target HP to `1`
  - removes `bleeding`, `dead`, `dying`, `unconscious`
  - only works on loaded character sheets, not transient summons
  - mana cost is hardcoded `6`

Passive/cantrip implementation:
- melee skill bonus from cantrip is handled in the passive provider
- undead aggro behavior is also added there as utility traits

- Summons:

- current model is more ad hoc around summon options and old summon templates

### 407. Assistant

`Shadow Control` currently has:

- spells:
  - `Cloak of Shadow`
  - `Shadow Walk`
  - `Shadow Manipulation`
  - `Shadow Soldier`
  - current extra runtime action: `Dismiss Summon`
- passive/cantrip:
  - cosmetic clothing/armor shift
  - minor body cosmetics at level 5
  - `Shadow Walk` utility trait shown in passive output

Action classes:

- parent classes:
  - `AuraSpellAction`
  - `UtilitySpellAction`
  - `AttackSpellAction`
  - `SummonSpellAction`
- children:
  - `CloakOfShadowSpellAction`
  - `ShadowWalkSpellAction`
  - `ShadowManipulationSpellAction`
  - `ShadowSoldierSpellAction`

Effect classes:

- `Cloak of Shadow`
  - `AuraEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Shadow Walk`
  - `LogEffect` only
- `Shadow Manipulation`
  - `DamageEffect`
  - `LogEffect`
- `Shadow Soldier`
  - `SummonEffect`
  - sometimes `AuraEffect`
  - `LogEffect`

Behavior under current action/effect runtime:

- `CloakOfShadowSpellAction`
  - builds the cloak aura through `buildActivePowerEffect(...)`
  - self-only at lower levels
  - at level 4+, if cast in aura mode, also shares to allies
  - linked ally aura effects are added through `buildLinkedAuraEffectForTarget(...)`
  - logs the cast

- `ShadowWalkSpellAction`
  - utility/movement action
  - requires one living target
  - costs `2` mana
  - produces no direct state-change effect besides log output
  - current encounter runtime treats it as a logged movement-style action

- `ShadowManipulationSpellAction`
  - builds direct shadow damage through `buildDirectDamageCastResolution(...)`
  - auto-hit behavior comes from the power rules data
  - returns `DamageEffect`
  - logs the cast

- `ShadowSoldierSpellAction`
  - summons the level 5 shadow soldier through summon resolution
  - inherits active aura effects from the caster when relevant
  - `Dismiss Summon` is handled inside the same action class, but still exposed as a separate variant id

Passive/cantrip implementation:
- `ShadowControlPassiveProvider`
  - adds `Shadow Walk <range>` as utility trait from level 2
  - adds cosmetic clothing/armor shift from level 3
  - adds minor body cosmetics from level 5

### 410. Assistant

Quite different, but closer than some of the others.

- `Smoldering Shadow` vs current `Cloak of Shadow`:
  - broadly similar role
  - current also adds `Intimidation`; your version removes that
  - current durations are `10m / 10m / 10m / 60m / 60m`, not `15m / 30m / 1h / 2h / 4h`
  - current aura-sharing starts at L4, which matches the broad idea

- `Shadow Walk`:
  - very close
  - current is bonus action, mana `2`, range `25m x SC`
  - current does not have a separate `Shadow Walk and Attack` spell

- `Shadow Walk and Attack`:
  - missing entirely in current code
  - no surprise / temporary AC-loss mechanic exists for it

- `Shadow Manipulation`:
  - current is very close
  - same unlock at L3, same mana `2`, same damage pattern `MAN + SC`, same “counts as attack” intent
  - this is one of the better-aligned spells

- `Sleek Visage`:
  - current passive/cantrip is close
  - clothing/armor cosmetics at L3
  - minor body cosmetics at L5
  - so this is mostly aligned

- `Shadow Fighter`:
  - current `Shadow Soldier` is close in spirit
  - but current duration is not “until destroyed”; it is still tied to summon duration rules
  - current stats are simpler template-based values, not exactly `SCL + MAN`
  - current already supports buffable / not healable / shadow-cold immunity / physical resistance / radiant vulnerability style rules

Coding-wise:
- your version is cleaner
- biggest missing piece is `Shadow Walk and Attack`
- second major difference is your much clearer summon spec for `Shadow Fighter` and the removal of `Intimidation` from the cloak spell

### 443. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
# Knowledge Card System V1 Plan

## Summary
Implement a new standalone knowledge system where `History` stays a log and real knowledge lives in revisioned cards. V1 ships full end-to-end support for **character cards only**, including spell-generated cards from `Assess Character`, full **DM authoring/grant** flows, linked history UI, and a new inline full-width `Knowledge` manager on the character sheet. Old saved `intel_snapshot` test entries are removed during migration instead of being converted.

## Implementation Changes
### Types, storage, and persistence
- Add new top-level persisted collections alongside `characters` and `items`:
  - `knowledgeEntities`
  - `knowledgeRevisions`
  - `knowledgeOwnerships`
- Add generic domain types now, but only implement `character` subject behavior in v1:
  - `KnowledgeEntity`
  - `KnowledgeRevision`
  - `KnowledgeOwnership`
  - `KnowledgeRevisionSection`
  - `KnowledgeEntityType` with `character | item | place | faction | story | custom`
  - `KnowledgeSourceType` with at least `spell | share | manual_edit | dm_grant`
  - `KnowledgeLineageMode` with at least `observed | copied | edited_copy | updated_scan`
- Extend persisted app state and `AppFlow` context to hydrate, store, sync, and mutate the new collections through localStorage just like `items`.
- Do **not** embed card content inside `CharacterDraft`; ownership is resolved from the standalone ownership collection via `ownerCharacterId`.
- Add hydration migration that:
  - initializes missing knowledge collections to empty
  - removes legacy `gameHistory` entries of type `intel_snapshot` that contain the old embedded test snapshot model
  - preserves normal note history entries

### History model and card creation
- Keep `GameHistoryEntry` log-based, but make knowledge-related rows link to exact revisions:
  - add `knowledgeEntityId`
  - add `knowledgeRevisionId`
- Keep the existing `intel_snapshot` history row type name for compatibility/minimal churn, but stop using embedded snapshot content as the source of truth.
- Replace the current `Assess Character` write path so it:
  - finds or creates a `KnowledgeEntity` for the scanned character
  - builds a structured character-card payload from the same visible intel data already produced today
  - creates a new immutable `KnowledgeRevision`
  - creates `KnowledgeOwnership` for the caster
  - writes a linked history row pointing to that exact revision
- `Assess Character` revision rules:
  - first scan for a subject: `lineageMode = observed`, `sourceType = spell`, `isCanonical = true`
  - later scan of the same subject: `lineageMode = updated_scan`, `sourceType = spell`, `isCanonical = true`
  - revision number increments per entity
- V1 character-card content sections:
  - summary
  - biography
  - resistances
  - combat summary
  - stats
  - skills
  - powers
  - specials
  - notes

### Knowledge operations and ownership rules
- Add mutation helpers/selectors for:
  - create entity if missing
  - create spell-generated revision
  - create snapshot-based DM revision
  - create freeform DM character card
  - duplicate revision
  - create edited copy
  - share revision
  - pin/unpin ownership
  - archive/unarchive ownership
  - rename ownership-local label
- Ownership rules:
  - a character may own many revisions of the same entity
  - many characters may own the same revision
  - sharing reuses the same revision by default
  - duplicating or editing creates a new revision plus new ownership
  - `localLabel`, `isPinned`, and `isArchived` live on `KnowledgeOwnership`
- DM authoring in v1:
  - available in `dm-editable` sheet view
  - supports snapshot-based card generation from the currently viewed character
  - supports freeform manual character-card creation
  - supports editing title, summary, and section content before saving
  - supports granting to one or more selected characters
- Revision defaults:
  - DM snapshot/manual grant from current viewed character: `sourceType = dm_grant`
  - freeform/manual DM edits based on an existing revision: `lineageMode = edited_copy`, `isCanonical = false`
  - plain duplicate: `lineageMode = copied`, `isCanonical = false`

## UI Changes
### History UI
- Keep `Session Notes` behavior unchanged.
- Upgrade `Game History` rows so linked intel rows are interactive:
  - hover opens a lightweight preview popover
  - click opens the full card revision in a modal
- Preview content should show:
  - card title
  - revision label
  - short summary
  - provenance/source label
- Non-linked note rows remain plain text.
- This work **absorbs** `CS-HIST-01`; do not build a separate old-style raw snapshot renderer.

### Knowledge manager on the character sheet
- Add a new **full-width inline `Knowledge` section** as a sibling section on the existing sheet page.
- Render it in all sheet modes:
  - player
  - dm-readonly
  - dm-editable
- Disable mutating actions in read-only modes.
- Use a 3-pane inline layout:
  - left: owned subjects/entities
  - middle: owned revisions for selected subject
  - right: selected revision detail
- Default organization:
  - subjects grouped by `KnowledgeEntity`
  - revisions sorted newest-first
  - archived ownerships hidden by default behind a toggle
  - pinned ownerships surfaced first
- Player-side v1 actions in the manager:
  - open
  - duplicate
  - create edited copy
  - share
  - archive / unarchive
  - pin / unpin
  - rename local label
  - compare two revisions of the same subject
- Comparison UI:
  - side-by-side revision comparison inside the Knowledge section detail pane
  - compare only revisions of the same entity
- History click target and Knowledge open action should reuse the same full-card modal/detail component.

## Test Plan
- Persistence and migration
  - hydrating old storage without knowledge collections yields empty collections
  - legacy embedded `intel_snapshot` rows are removed
  - normal note history survives migration
  - knowledge collections persist and sync through localStorage events
- Domain behavior
  - `Assess Character` creates entity, revision, ownership, and linked history row
  - repeated scans create later revisions on the same entity
  - duplicate creates a new non-canonical revision
  - edited copy preserves lineage to parent revision
  - share adds ownership without cloning by default
  - pin/archive/local label only affect ownership, not revision content
- UI behavior
  - history hover preview appears only for linked knowledge rows
  - clicking a linked history row opens the exact revision
  - Knowledge section groups by subject and lists revisions correctly
  - compare mode renders two revisions of the same entity side-by-side
  - read-only views can browse but cannot mutate
  - DM-editable view can snapshot-create, freeform-create, edit, and grant cards
- Acceptance scenarios
  - player uses `Assess Character` and immediately sees a linked history row plus the new card in `Knowledge`
  - player duplicates/edits/shares a card and the recipient sees it on their own sheet
  - DM creates a manual character card and grants it to selected characters
  - old test intel history data is gone after loading the new build

## Assumptions
- V1 supports **character cards only** end-to-end; item/story/place/faction cards use the same architecture later.
- V1 includes the **full manager** now: duplicate, edited copy, share, archive, pin, local rename, and compare.
- V1 includes **full DM authoring now**: snapshot-based creation, freeform manual creation, edit-before-save, and grant flows.
- Old saved `Assess Character` embedded intel rows are intentionally discarded during migration.
- Main knowledge UI stays inline on the current sheet page, not on a new route or tab.
</proposed_plan>
