### 537. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
# ARCH-REM-01 Plan

## Summary
Extract the encounter execute/advance/upkeep/cleanup logic out of `CombatEncounterPage.tsx` into a **class-based encounter engine** while keeping the current `PreparedCastRequest` contract, current UI flows, current save shape, and current spell behavior unchanged. This refactor does **not** include aura architecture redesign; aura spells stay on the current builder/shape for now.

## Key Changes
- Introduce a new `EncounterExecutionEngine` class as the single runtime entrypoint for the post-prepare phase.
- Keep request preparation where it is now:
  - `prepareCastRequest`
  - `preparePhysicalAttackRequest`
  - `prepareBruteDefianceRequest`
- Keep `PreparedCastRequest` as the execution input type. Do not redesign spell/action APIs in this refactor.
- Add an engine result type, for example `EncounterExecutionResult`, that returns:
  - updated `encounter`
  - updated `characters`
  - any derived UI-facing side outputs needed by the route
- Move these responsibilities out of the route and into engine methods:
  - prepared request execution
  - resource/status/usage-counter application
  - healing and damage application
  - crowd-control break detection and immunity application
  - summon add/replace/dismiss handling
  - ongoing-state add/remove/release handling
  - history entry application
  - knowledge card creation from linked `Assess Character` rows
  - turn advancement
  - upkeep spending
  - aura cleanup on source death
  - encounter log generation tied to advance/upkeep
- Keep `CombatEncounterPage.tsx` as orchestration/UI only:
  - build request
  - ask for confirmations if needed
  - call engine
  - commit returned state
- Use one main class with clear public methods:
  - `executePreparedRequest(request)`
  - `advanceTurn()`
- Keep the rest as private methods or engine-local helpers, not extra public architecture.

## Incremental Delivery
1. Extract route-local helper logic into the engine class without changing behavior:
   - character/sheet resolution
   - status and usage-counter application
   - structural merge helpers
2. Move prepared request execution into `EncounterExecutionEngine.executePreparedRequest()`:
   - route wrappers call the engine but keep current UI flow unchanged
3. Move turn advancement and upkeep into `EncounterExecutionEngine.advanceTurn()`:
   - includes maintained control spending, aura cleanup, summon/ongoing cleanup, and log output
4. Remove obsolete duplicated route logic and leave the page as a thin coordinator

## Test Plan
- Keep passing:
  - `npm run typecheck`
  - `npm test`
  - `npm run build`
- Add engine-focused tests for:
  - prepared request execution updates encounter + characters correctly
  - healing/damage/resource/status/usage-counter application parity
  - crowd-control break and immunity behavior
  - summon add/replace/dismiss behavior
  - linked `Assess Character` execution still creates knowledge revisions and linked history rows
  - turn advance upkeep spending and cleanup parity
- Preserve existing combat regression coverage for:
  - casting
  - physical attacks
  - `Brute Defiance`
  - encounter snapshot behavior
  - knowledge/history integration from combat

## Assumptions
- `PreparedCastRequest` remains the stable boundary for this refactor.
- Aura-builder redesign is explicitly out of scope for `ARCH-REM-01`.
- No spell redesign TODO is folded into this work.
- The class-based engine should still behave like a deterministic state transformer; no hidden global state or React dependencies inside it.
</proposed_plan>

<proposed_plan>
# Remaining Power TODO Plan

## Summary
Implement the remaining active power TODOs as a staged series of behavior-change passes on top of the current `Action` / `Effect` runtime and the new `EncounterExecutionEngine`. Keep `KNOW-V2-01`, `AURA-ARCH-DISCUSS-01`, and `B01` deferred and untouched except for tracking hygiene. Do not do another architecture rewrite during this pass; change power behavior, spell structure, passives, UI labels/options, and tests only.

## Implementation Changes
### Stage 0: Tracking and safety
- Move these items to deferred and leave them there:
  - `KNOW-V2-01`
  - `AURA-ARCH-DISCUSS-01`
  - `B01`
- Keep `references/plan.md` aligned with the active implementation order below.
- Preserve current local save compatibility and `PreparedCastRequest` boundary.

### Stage 1: `BR-BD-01`
- Replace manual `Brute Defiance` trigger behavior with the passive delayed stand-up model:
  - trigger only when HP is `0` to `-5`
  - enqueue a `body_reinforcement_revive` ongoing state instead of immediate HP restore
  - resolve after one turn advance
  - 1/day
  - HP scaling `1 / 2 / 4 / 8 / 16`
- Update encounter UI so `Brute Defiance` is no longer a manual action button.
- Keep `Boost Physique` unchanged in this stage.

### Stage 2: `CC-CE-01`, `CC-PASSIVE-01`, `CC-PASSIVE-02`
- Remove `release_control` as a user-facing spell choice.
- Keep `Control Entity (CE)` as the only `Crowd Control` spell.
- Add a contextual release/control-management action in encounter UI for already controlled targets.
- Replace the current passive provider output with:
  - `Crowd Management (CM)`: `Social + power level`
  - `Compulsion Guard (CG)`: at level `5`, add `Social` while defending against control effects
- Keep current control contest, upkeep, immunity-on-break, and ongoing-state behavior unless explicitly changed by the new spell spec.

### Stage 3: `ELM-SPELL-01`
- Split `Elementalist` into 3 explicit spells:
  - `Elemental Bolt`
  - `Elemental Cantrip`
  - `Elemental Split`
- Replace the single `ElementalistSpellAction` branch model with one concrete action class per spell.
- Remove split-style behavior from `Elemental Bolt` and move it to `Elemental Split`.
- Enforce the explicit cantrip rules, including:
  - no necrotic
  - separate level-based targeting/action behavior
  - no hidden inheritance from `Elemental Bolt`

### Stage 4: `HEAL-SPELL-01`
- Rename and separate `Healing` into 3 explicit spells:
  - `Heal Living (HL)`
  - `Holy Purge (HP)`
  - `Healing Touch (HT)`
- Replace the single `HealingSpellAction` branch model with one concrete action class per spell.
- Keep undead-healing inversion behavior unless the final spell spec says otherwise.
- Keep overheal, bleeding stop, cleanse, and limb-regrowth logic attached to the correct new spell only.

### Stage 5: `LS-SPELL-01`
- Replace the compressed `Light Support` structure with:
  - `Let There Be Light (LTBL)`
  - `Lunar Bless (LB)`
  - `Lessen Darkness (LD)`
  - `Luminous Restoration (LR)`
- Keep aura implementation on the current builder path; do not split aura architecture in this pass.
- Make `LD` an explicit linked level-5 effect rather than implicit folded behavior.
- Move passive mana/nightvision scaling into the updated passive provider.

### Stage 6: `NECRO-SPELL-01`
- Rework `Necromancy` to:
  - `Non-Living Warriors (NW)` as the summon parent concept
  - explicit summon children `NS`, `NSK`, `NZ`
  - `Necrotic Touch (NT)`
  - `Necromancer's Bless (NB)`
  - `Necromancer's Deception (ND)`
- Keep dismiss/removal as internal summon-management behavior, not a separate user-facing spell.
- Replace current summon templates and passive progression with the newer formulas/rules.

### Stage 7: `SC-SPELL-01`
- Rework `Shadow Control` to:
  - `Smoldering Shadow (SS)`
  - `Shadow Walk (SW)`
  - `Shadow Walk and Attack (SWaA)`
  - `Shadow Manipulation (SM)`
  - `Sleek Visage (SV)`
  - `Shadow Fighter (SF)`
- Add `SWaA` as a real separate spell/action.
- Replace the current cloak passive/effect names and summon spec with the newer version.
- Keep dismiss/removal as summon-management behavior, not a separate spell.

## Public Interfaces / Types
- Update spell ids, labels, and selectable variant lists in the power registry/runtime support so the encounter UI exposes the new spell sets.
- Update passive provider outputs for `Crowd Control`, `Light Support`, `Necromancy`, and `Shadow Control` to match the new passive lines.
- Update any usage-counter keys only where the new spell behavior requires separate tracking; keep existing keys when behavior is unchanged enough to preserve save compatibility.
- Keep `PreparedCastRequest`, encounter state shape, and persisted character/item/knowledge storage compatible unless a behavior change absolutely requires a new key.

## Test Plan
- After each stage run:
  - `npm run typecheck`
  - `npm test`
  - `npm run build`
- Extend targeted tests by subsystem:
  - `tests/combatEncounterSpecialActions.test.ts` for `Brute Defiance`
  - `tests/combatEncounterCasting.test.ts` for spell availability, targeting, upkeep/release, summon behavior, and damage/healing rules
  - `tests/powerRegistry.test.ts` for new spell ids and action-class mapping
  - `tests/characterRuntime.test.ts` for passive-provider changes
  - `tests/powerEffects.test.ts` where spell-resolution helpers still drive the new rules
- Add acceptance scenarios for:
  - passive delayed `Brute Defiance`
  - contextual `Control Entity` release
  - `Elemental Split` as a real separate spell
  - `HL / HP / HT` separation
  - explicit `LTBL / LB / LD / LR`
  - explicit `NW / NS / NSK / NZ / NT / NB / ND`
  - explicit `SS / SW / SWaA / SM / SV / SF`

## Assumptions
- Implementation order is:
  1. `BR-BD-01`
  2. `CC-CE-01`, `CC-PASSIVE-01`, `CC-PASSIVE-02`
  3. `ELM-SPELL-01`
  4. `HEAL-SPELL-01`
  5. `LS-SPELL-01`
  6. `NECRO-SPELL-01`
  7. `SC-SPELL-01`
- Deferred items remain deferred:
  - `KNOW-V2-01`
  - `AURA-ARCH-DISCUSS-01`
  - `B01`
- No new architecture track is introduced during this pass; this is a power/spec rewrite pass on the current engine.
</proposed_plan>

## My request for Codex:
i am looking actions in combat encounter. some actions work with `select powers > select spell > select target` principle. some different, like `select power > select target`. so there is no standardization. is this normal? should we be normilizing/standardizing the behaviours?

### 634. Assistant

Yes, you should standardize it.

My recommendation:
- always keep the same outer flow: `select power -> select spell/mechanic -> select target -> confirm`
- even when a power has only one spell, show either:
  - an explicit single spell choice, or
  - auto-select it but keep the UI structure logically the same

Why:
- it reduces cognitive switching
- it makes the encounter UI easier to maintain
- it prevents special-case UI logic from spreading

Short version:
- internal mechanics can differ
- user-facing interaction flow should be standardized

### 635. Assistant

Yes, you should standardize it.

My recommendation:
- always keep the same outer flow: `select power -> select spell/mechanic -> select target -> confirm`

Why:
- it reduces cognitive switching
- it makes the encounter UI easier to maintain
- it prevents special-case UI logic from spreading

Short version:
- internal mechanics can differ
- user-facing interaction flow should be standardized

### 648. Assistant

Current combat-encounter spell map:

- `Awareness / Assess Character`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; single target, `0` mana, checks CR limit, then writes an encounter log plus a linked knowledge/history card.
- `Body Reinforcement / Boost Physique`: `select power -> select target -> select stat`; one friendly target, choose `STR/DEX/STAM`, applies a buff effect.
- `Body Reinforcement / Brute Defiance`: passive, not selectable; if HP is between `0` and `-5`, it auto-queues a revive after one turn, `1/day`, restoring `1 / 2 / 4 / 8 / 16` HP by level.
- `Crowd Control / Control Entity`: `select power -> select spell -> select target(s)`; enemy control spell, auto-resolves contest, applies `Paralyzed` + `Controlled by <caster>` and creates upkeep state.
- `Crowd Control / Release`: not a normal spell; contextual action for already controlled targets, removes control/paralysis and ends the maintained state.
- `Elementalist / Elemental Bolt`: `select power -> select spell -> select target -> select damage type`; single-target direct damage, low levels lock first chosen element until long rest, `necrotic` unlocks at level 5 and heals undead instead of damaging them.
- `Elementalist / Elemental Cantrip`: `select power -> select spell -> select target(s) -> select damage type`; `0` mana, elemental only, up to `3` targets at level 5.
- `Elementalist / Elemental Split`: `select power -> select spell -> select targets -> select damage type -> choose bonus mana`; explicit multi-target split spell, extra mana boosts split damage.
- `Healing / Heal Living`: `select power -> select spell -> select target(s)`; heals living targets, removes bleeding, supports multi-target healing allocation, can regrow limbs, and can overheal to temp HP at high level. Against undead it becomes radiant damage.
- `Healing / Holy Purge`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; cleanse spell, removes poison/disease/curse, no normal HP heal. Against undead, any heal amount is reversed into radiant damage.
- `Healing / Healing Touch`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; smaller heal, stops bleeding, `2/day` per target. Against undead, it also reverses into radiant damage.
- `Light Support / Let There Be Light`: `select power -> select spell`; self-cast aura source, then automatically applies allied aura buffs from the caster.
- `Light Support / Luminous Restoration`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; restores friendly target mana, scaling by `APP`.
- `Light Support / Lessen Darkness`: `select power -> select spell`; requires an active `Let There Be Light` source on the caster, then applies linked enemy debuff effects from that aura.
- `Necromancy / Non-Living Skeleton`: `select power -> select spell`; summon spell, spawns that summon subtype near the caster and can inherit active aura effects.
- `Necromancy / Non-Living Zombie`: same flow as above, different summon subtype.
- `Necromancy / Non-Living Skeleton King`: same flow as above, different summon subtype.
- `Necromancy / Necrotic Touch`: `select power -> select spell -> select target -> resolve hit/miss`; on hit it deals necrotic damage, heals the caster by necromancy level, and heals undead targets instead of damaging them.
- `Necromancy / Necromancer's Bless`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; resurrection-style spell, sets target to `1 HP` and removes `bleeding/dead/dying/unconscious`.
- `Necromancy / Dismiss summon`: internal/contextual summon-management action, not a normal visible spell.
- `Shadow Control / Smoldering Shadow`: `select power -> select spell`, and at higher level also choose `self/aura`; applies stealth + AC aura effects.
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Walk`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; movement-style spell, logs the move, no direct damage effect.
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Walk and Attack`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; separate ambush action. Right now it logs the ambush; it does not auto-resolve the follow-up attack by itself.
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Manipulation`: `select power -> select spell -> select target`; direct shadow damage spell.
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Fighter`: `select power -> select spell`; summon spell, spawns near caster and can inherit aura effects.
- `Shadow Control / Dismiss summon`: internal/contextual summon-management action, not a normal visible spell.

Short pattern summary:
- Most now use `power -> spell -> target`.
- Self-only aura/summon spells often stop at `power -> spell`.
- A few need extra inputs: `stat`, `damage type`, `bonus mana`, `hit/miss`, `healing allocation`, or `self/aura mode`.

## My request for Codex:
i did not mean the mechanics on the backend, i mean the mechanics on UI. canyou please map out the UI mechanics, what a user sees and interacts with. if user actively selects power but not spell, and then target, show in your mapping: `power > target` only even if it works `power > spell > target` on the background.

### 651. Assistant

### 652. Assistant

### 653. Assistant

### 654. Assistant

I found the actual cast form component; I’m opening that directly to match the field order users see in the encounter UI.

### 655. Assistant

Yes. UI-wise, the cast form is basically:

`Power > Action (if shown) > Target(s) (if shown) > special field(s) > Cast Selected Power`

`Action` only appears when that power has more than one visible spell at that level.

Current UI map:

- `Awareness / Assess Character`: `Power > Target`
- `Body Reinforcement / Boost Physique`: `Power > Target > Stat`
- `Body Reinforcement / Brute Defiance`: no cast UI; passive only
- `Crowd Control / Control Entity`: `Power > Target(s)`
- `Crowd Control / Release`: not in cast form; contextual release action on already controlled targets

- `Elementalist / Elemental Bolt`: `Power > Target > Damage Type` when it is the only visible spell; otherwise `Power > Action > Target > Damage Type`
- `Elementalist / Elemental Cantrip`: `Power > Action > Target > Damage Type` or `Power > Action > Targets > Damage Type` at higher level
- `Elementalist / Elemental Split`: `Power > Action > Targets > Damage Type > Extra Mana`

- `Healing / Heal Living`: `Power > Target(s) > Healing Allocation` when it is the only visible spell; otherwise `Power > Action > Target(s) > Healing Allocation`
- `Healing / Holy Purge`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Healing / Healing Touch`: `Power > Action > Target`

- `Light Support / Let There Be Light`: `Power` when it is the only visible spell; otherwise `Power > Action`
- `Light Support / Luminous Restoration`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Light Support / Lessen Darkness`: `Power > Action`

- `Necromancy / Non-Living Skeleton`: `Power > Summon` when it is the only visible spell; otherwise `Power > Action > Summon`
- `Necromancy / Non-Living Zombie`: `Power > Action > Summon`
- `Necromancy / Non-Living Skeleton King`: `Power > Action > Summon`
- `Necromancy / Necrotic Touch`: `Power > Action > Target > Touch Attack`
- `Necromancy / Necromancer’s Bless`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Necromancy / dismiss summon`: not cast form; contextual summon-management action

- `Shadow Control / Smoldering Shadow`: `Power` when it is the only visible spell; later `Power > Action`, and at aura-capable levels `Power > Action > Mode`
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Walk`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Walk and Attack`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Manipulation`: `Power > Action > Target`
- `Shadow Control / Shadow Fighter`: `Power > Action > Summon`
- `Shadow Control / dismiss summon`: not cast form; contextual summon-management action

Special visible UI fields that exist right now:
- `Stat`: only for `Boost Physique`
- `Damage Type`: `Elementalist`
- `Extra Mana`: `Elemental Split`
- `Touch Attack`: `Necrotic Touch`
- `Healing Allocation`: `Heal Living`
- `Mode`: `Smoldering Shadow`
- `Summon`: `Necromancy` summon spells and `Shadow Fighter`

If you want, I can next turn this into a “what should be standardized” list.

- `Necromancy / Non-Living Skeleton` at low level: `Power > Summon`

- `Crowd Control / Release`: contextual action, not cast-form spell selection
- `Necromancy / dismiss summon`: contextual summon-management action
- `Shadow Control / dismiss summon`: contextual summon-management action
- `Body Reinforcement / Brute Defiance`: passive, no cast UI

- standardize active-cast UI to always show `Power > Spell ...`
- for self-only spells, standard form becomes `Power > Spell`
- handle contextual mechanics separately after that, because they are not normal spells in the same sense

### 663. Assistant

Yes. Your normalization target is coherent.

What I’d record as the desired UI standard:
- always show `Power > Spell`
- then show only the extra fields that spell actually needs:
  - `Target`
  - `Targets`
  - `Mode`
  - `Stat`
  - `Damage Type`
  - `Summon`
  - `Touch Attack`
  - `Healing Allocation`

So your revised irregulars become:
- `Awareness`: `Power > Spell > Target`
- `Body Reinforcement`: `Power > Spell > Target > Stat`
- `Elementalist / Elemental Bolt`: always `Power > Spell > Target > Damage Type`
- `Healing / Heal Living`: always `Power > Spell > Target(s)` and then allocation panel if needed
- `Light Support / Let There Be Light`: `Power > Spell > Target(s)`
- `Necromancy`: `Power > Spell(Non-Living Warriors) > Summon(child)`
- `Shadow Control / Smoldering Shadow`: always `Power > Spell > Mode`

And your contextual notes are correct:
- `Crowd Control / Release`: keep contextual, not cast-form spell UI
- `Necromancy / dismiss summon`: currently supported internally, but not exposed in visible UI
- `Shadow Control / dismiss summon`: same; it exists internally, but there is no visible spell/action for it now
- `Body Reinforcement / Brute Defiance`: passive-only is correct

So the real issues to discuss next are:
- cast-form standardization
- whether aura spells should visibly target allies in the cast UI
- where summon dismiss should live in the encounter UI

## My request for Codex:
1. first of all, let's add these standardization notes todo
2. add dismiss summon mechanics to the UI both for necro and SC. make it similar to CC's release  mechanics (if not like that already). -> do not implement yet, add necessary notes todo
3. aura spells originated from the caster. when caster stops/cancells the aura spell benefitting targets should lose it too. that is what makes aura spells different than the targetted spells. in current mechanics, if i cancel the aura spell from the caster, it does not affect the benefitter target (targetted characters still have it). with this knowledge, if you think that we should create a new spell class (aura), let's do it; fi you think that we can manage it with its current method under targetted spells (it is lighter this way, it is easier this way, etc..., whatever) we should do it that way then. you play the expert role and make the design decision. if need be a change/update, add that todo list - no implementation yet.
4. cast-form standardization: what's that? you need to explain it first.
5. whether aura spells should visibly target allies in the cast UI: what do you mean? regardless aura spell or not, targetting is and will be a part of buffs. even aura spells can exlude allies, or include enemies (party members, or opposing party members), because the concept of ally and enemy is in the eye of the caster, not the group or something else. the caster can change a status of alliance in the middle of a combat, hence that will effect the benefitters of the caster's aura. that is why aura spells still needs targetting. yet, caveat of aura spells, in comparison to targetted buffs, is targetted buffs are target specific and once cast, the target owns it, benefits from it and cannot be cancelled by the caster, however, aura spells are caster specific (originated from the caster), hence can be removed from the benefitting targets by the caster, or in case of caster losing the aura, targets of the aura loses the aura effects as well.
6. where summon dismiss should live in the encounter UI: as i explained it should live in the caster's action menu, similar to 'release' concept of CC.

### 670. Assistant

1. Added as active TODOs in [tasks_todo.md](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/project_tracking/tasks_todo.md):
- `CAST-UI-STD-01`
- `SUMMON-UI-01`
- `AURA-LIFECYCLE-01`

I also updated [current_notes.md](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/current_notes.md) and [task_log.md](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/project_tracking/task_log.md).

2. `Dismiss Summon` is now recorded as a UI TODO for both `Necromancy` and `Shadow Control`, and the note says it should live in the caster’s action menu like `Crowd Control` release. Not implemented yet.

3. My design decision: keep aura spells as dedicated aura spells. We already have `AuraSpellAction`; the problem is not “missing class,” it is wrong aura lifecycle/target ownership, so I added `AURA-LIFECYCLE-01` for:
- explicit aura target selection in UI
- source-linked beneficiary effects
- canceling/removing the caster aura removes the beneficiaries’ aura effects too

4. `Cast-form standardization` means the visible encounter UI should follow one consistent interaction pattern. In practice: active casts should always start with `Power > Spell`, then show only the extra fields that spell needs, instead of sometimes skipping the `Spell` step and sometimes not.

5. On aura targeting: I agree with you. Aura spells still need target selection; they are not “party auto-buffs.” The difference from targeted buffs is ownership/lifecycle: targeted buffs belong to the target once cast, while aura effects belong to the caster’s source and should disappear from beneficiaries when the source is canceled or lost.

6. On summon dismiss: agreed. It should live in the caster’s encounter action menu as a contextual action, not as a normal spell in the cast form.

No validation run; this was doc/tracking only.

### 680. Assistant

My suggestion:

**Method**
1. `Source text`
- your raw docs/txt

2. `Normalization pass`
- we rewrite each `power` and each `spell` into a fixed checklist
- we mark fields as:
  - `required`
  - `recommended`
  - `optional`

3. `Validation pass`
- if a missing field blocks coding or UI, we ask you
- if it does not block anything, we leave it blank/default and note it

4. `Canonical JSON`
- one standard JSON format for every `power` and `spell`

5. `Implementation pass`
- JSON -> runtime rules
- JSON -> combat UI fields
- JSON -> tests

**Best rule**
Only ask follow-up questions for `blocking` gaps.

**Blocking fields for a spell**
- `name`
- `powerId`
- `unlockLevel`
- `active/passive`
- `spell category`
- `targeting`
- `range`
- `mana cost`
- `duration`
- `main mechanical effect`
- `level scaling`
- `special constraints`
- `if aura/summon/control`: upkeep/cancel/source-link behavior

**Non-blocking fields**
- flavor text
- lore text
- cosmetic notes
- example uses

**Suggested JSON shape**
```json
{
  "power": {
    "id": "awareness",
    "name": "Awareness",
    "abbr": "AW",
    "governingStat": "PER",
    "spells": [
      {
        "id": "assess_character",
        "name": "Assess Character",
        "abbr": "AC",
        "kind": "knowledge",
        "mode": "active",
        "unlockLevel": 1,
        "actionCost": "bonus",
        "manaCost": 0,
        "range": "line_of_sight",
        "duration": "instant",
        "targeting": {
          "targetMode": "single",
          "targetType": ["character"]
        },
        "scaling": {
          "1": {},
          "2": {},
          "3": {}
        },
        "mechanics": {
          "createsKnowledgeCard": true,
          "writesHistoryLink": true
        },
        "constraints": [],
        "notes": []
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

**Important design choice**
Do not store only prose in JSON.
Store:
- normalized fields
- structured mechanics
- explicit level overrides

**Process I recommend**
- `Step 1`: define the canonical JSON schema
- `Step 2`: define the blocking-vs-non-blocking validator rules
- `Step 3`: create one worked example with a new `power`
- `Step 4`: use that as the ingestion template for all future `powers`

If you want, next I can draft the **exact standard JSON schema v1** for this project.

### 681. Assistant

My suggestion:

**Method**
1. `Source text`
- your raw docs/txt

2. `Normalization pass`
- we rewrite each `power` and each `spell` into a fixed checklist
- we mark fields as:
  - `required`
  - `recommended`
  - `optional`

3. `Validation pass`
- if a missing field blocks coding or UI, we ask you
- if it does not block anything, we leave it blank/default and note it

4. `Canonical JSON`
- one standard JSON format for every `power` and `spell`

5. `Implementation pass`
- JSON -> runtime rules
- JSON -> combat UI fields
- JSON -> tests

**Best rule**
Only ask follow-up questions for `blocking` gaps.

**Blocking fields for a spell**
- `name`
- `powerId`
- `unlockLevel`
- `active/passive`
- `spell category`
- `targeting`
- `range`
- `mana cost`
- `duration`
- `main mechanical effect`
- `level scaling`
- `special constraints`
- `if aura/summon/control`: upkeep/cancel/source-link behavior

**Non-blocking fields**
- flavor text
- lore text
- cosmetic notes
- example uses

**Suggested JSON shape**
```json
{
  "power": {
    "id": "awareness",
    "name": "Awareness",
    "abbr": "AW",
    "governingStat": "PER",
    "spells": [
      {
        "id": "assess_character",
        "name": "Assess Character",
        "abbr": "AC",
        "kind": "knowledge",
        "mode": "active",
        "unlockLevel": 1,
        "actionCost": "bonus",
        "manaCost": 0,
        "range": "line_of_sight",
        "duration": "instant",
        "targeting": {
          "targetMode": "single",
          "targetType": ["character"]
        },
        "scaling": {
          "1": {},
          "2": {},
          "3": {}
        },
        "mechanics": {
          "createsKnowledgeCard": true,
          "writesHistoryLink": true
        },
        "constraints": [],
        "notes": []
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

**Important design choice**
Do not store only prose in JSON.
Store:
- normalized fields
- structured mechanics
- explicit level overrides

**Process I recommend**
- `Step 1`: define the canonical JSON schema
- `Step 2`: define the blocking-vs-non-blocking validator rules
- `Step 3`: create one worked example with a new `power`
- `Step 4`: use that as the ingestion template for all future `powers`

If you want, next I can draft the **exact standard JSON schema v1** for this project.

## My request for Codex:
   not yet. one more thing. we created spell classes. i was thinking (and tell me if this is doable or not) to create a new parent for powers and spells, one for each. that would standardize them. i am planning make this final json file a feeder to the parent classess. so what would you say for thihs idea?

### 683. Assistant

Yes, doable.

And I think it is a good idea, if kept light.

What I would suggest:
- add a `PowerDefinition` parent/base model
- add a `SpellDefinition` parent/base model

Not heavy runtime classes for gameplay execution.
More like:
- standardized definition objects/classes
- fed by JSON
- used to validate, register, and expose powers/spells consistently

So the split becomes:

- `PowerDefinition` / `SpellDefinition`
  - metadata
  - validation
  - UI exposure
  - level scaling data
  - targeting/action/mana/duration definitions

- action/effect classes
  - actual encounter execution logic

That is the cleanest version.

So:
- JSON feeds `PowerDefinition` and `SpellDefinition`
- those definitions feed:
  - registry
  - UI
  - validation
- action/effect classes execute mechanics

My opinion:
- yes, do it
- but keep them as definition-layer parents, not giant behavior-owning classes

## My request for Codex:

### 686. Assistant

Not in the cleanest design.

`PowerDefinition` and `SpellDefinition` should be parents of the definition layer, not of the action classes.

So better split is:

- definition layer
  - `PowerDefinition`
  - `SpellDefinition`

- execution layer
  - `Action`
  - `Effect`

Because:
- definitions describe what a `power` or `spell` is
- action classes describe what happens when a `spell` is used

So technically possible?
- yes

Would I recommend it?
- no, not for the current architecture

- vite.config.ts: vite.config.ts

## My request for Codex:
i am not following why you do not recommend it and it is not a good idea.

### 689. Assistant

Because they solve different problems.

- `SpellDefinition`
  - describes the spell
  - name
  - mana cost
  - targeting
  - duration
  - unlock level
  - scaling
  - UI fields

- `Action`
  - executes the spell in combat
  - applies effects
  - validates runtime conditions
  - creates logs/history/knowledge/summons/statuses

If you make `SpellDefinition` the parent of action classes, one class starts carrying both:
- static design data
- runtime execution behavior

That mixes two responsibilities.

So the problem is not “impossible.”
The problem is:
- less clean separation
- harder maintenance
- harder ingestion from JSON
- harder testing later

That is why I do not recommend it.

## My request for Codex:
will action classes pull their behaviour from these definition classes?

### 692. Assistant

Yes, that is the right model.

`SpellDefinition` should feed the action class.
So:

- `SpellDefinition` says:
  - what the spell costs
  - how it targets
  - what fields it needs
  - what scaling rules it has

- `Action` says:
  - given this definition and this combat state, what happens now

So action classes should use the definition layer as input, not inherit from it.

## My request for Codex:
let's go one by one. what will do each sections

### 702. Assistant

Section by section:

- `definitionStatus`
  - tracks whether the definition is usable yet
  - records blocking gaps, non-blocking gaps, assumptions, notes

- `source`
  - records where this power/spell definition came from
  - txt/doc source, version, author, ingest timestamp

- `power`
  - defines the `power` itself
  - id, name, abbreviation, governing stat, summary, broad tags

- `globalRules`
  - rules shared by the whole `power`
  - defaults or general constraints that may apply to all spells under it

- `spells[]`
  - list of all `spells` under that `power`

Inside each `spell`:

- core spell fields
  - identity and classification
  - name, abbreviation, active/passive, category, unlock level

- `combatUI`
  - defines what the user must see/select in encounter UI
  - spell step, target step, summon step, mode step, etc.

- `targeting`
  - defines who/what can be targeted and how

- `costs`
  - action cost, mana cost, bonus mana, usage limits

- `duration`
  - instant/passive/aura/timed/upkeep behavior

- `mechanics`
  - what the spell actually does
  - effects, statuses, resources, special rules, implementation notes

- `levelProgression`
  - what changes at each level

- `validation`
  - spell-specific missing info, warnings, open questions

If you want, we can start with `definitionStatus` first.

### 705. Assistant

Two clarifications:

- `definitionStatus`
  - this is not gameplay data
  - it is ingestion/workflow data
  - purpose: tell us whether the JSON is complete enough to code from
  - example:
    - `readyForImplementation: true` means we have enough info
    - `blockingMissingFields` means we cannot safely implement yet
    - `nonBlockingMissingFields` means we can still proceed
    - `assumptions` stores the assumptions we made while normalizing the text

- spell `identity and classification`
  - `identity` = what exact spell this is
    - `id`, `name`, `abbreviation`
  - `classification` = what kind of spell it is in the system
    - `mode`: active/passive
    - `category`: attack, buff, aura, summon, knowledge, restoration, utility, control
    - `spellRole`: standalone / parent / child
    - `parentSpellId`: if this spell belongs under another spell concept like `Non-Living Warriors`

Current v1:

```json
{
  "schemaVersion": "power-spell-definition-v1",
  "definitionStatus": {
    "state": "draft",
    "readyForImplementation": false,
    "blockingMissingFields": [],
    "nonBlockingMissingFields": [],
    "assumptions": [],
    "notes": []
  },
  "source": {
    "documents": [],
    "sourceTextVersion": "",
    "ingestedAt": "",
    "author": ""
  },
  "power": {
    "id": "power_id",

### 706. Assistant

Two clarifications:

- `definitionStatus`
  - this is not gameplay data
  - it is ingestion/workflow data
  - purpose: tell us whether the JSON is complete enough to code from
  - example:
    - `readyForImplementation: true` means we have enough info
    - `blockingMissingFields` means we cannot safely implement yet
    - `nonBlockingMissingFields` means we can still proceed
    - `assumptions` stores the assumptions we made while normalizing the text

- spell `identity and classification`
  - `identity` = what exact spell this is
    - `id`, `name`, `abbreviation`
  - `classification` = what kind of spell it is in the system
    - `mode`: active/passive
    - `category`: attack, buff, aura, summon, knowledge, restoration, utility, control
    - `spellRole`: standalone / parent / child
    - `parentSpellId`: if this spell belongs under another spell concept like `Non-Living Warriors`

Current v1:

### 707. User

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: references/power_spell_definition_v1.json

## Open tabs:
- power_spell_definition_v1.json: references/power_spell_definition_v1.json
- T1 Supernatural Powers_v1.0.txt: retired_files/T1 Supernatural Powers_v1.0.txt
- T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt: references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt
- awareness.ts: src/powers/awareness.ts
- vite.config.ts: vite.config.ts

## My request for Codex:
1. `    "abbreviation": "PW",` what's this?
2. to what will abbreviation, theme, tags serve?
3. ```    "sharedRulesText": [],
    "sharedConstraints": [],
    "sharedKeywords": [], ``` what are these, what will they do? give me examples from current powers and spells to these and to this section (globalRules). this section feels a little overkill to me. prove me i am wrong.
4. ```      "parentSpellId": null,
      "spellRole": "standalone",
      "mode": "active",
      "category": "attack",
``` what are these for? again, give me examples to show why they will be useful.

### 708. Assistant

1. `"abbreviation": "PW"` is just a placeholder for the `power` abbreviation.
Example:
- `Awareness` -> `AW`
- `Body Reinforcement` -> `BR`
- `Crowd Control` -> `CC`

2. What these are for:
- `abbreviation`
  - useful for compact UI, logs, and formulas
  - example: `CC Lv 5`, `AW Lv 3`
- `theme`
  - broad flavor/domain label like `shadow`, `light`, `healing`, `necrotic`
  - mostly optional
- `tags`
  - machine-friendly labels for filtering/grouping
  - example:
    - `Smoldering Shadow` -> `["aura", "buff", "shadow"]`
    - `Necrotic Touch` -> `["attack", "necrotic", "life-drain"]`

My opinion:
- keep `abbreviation`
- `theme` and `tags` are optional and can be cut from v1 if you want a leaner schema

3. On `globalRules`:
You are mostly right. As written, it is too heavy.

What is useful:
- a small place for rules/defaults shared by many spells under one `power`

What feels too much:
- `sharedKeywords`
- probably also the current split between `sharedRulesText` and `sharedConstraints`

Examples where a light `globalRules` could help:
- `Elementalist`
  - many spells share `25m` range
  - many spells share elemental damage concepts
- `Light Support`
  - aura-related rules may be shared by multiple spells under that power
- `Necromancy`
  - not very useful at whole-power level
  - shared summon rules are better under a parent spell like `Non-Living Warriors`

So my recommendation:
- keep `globalRules`, but simplify it hard
- maybe reduce it to:
  - `sharedDefaults`
  - `sharedNotes`

4. These fields:
- `parentSpellId`
  - links a child spell to a parent spell family
  - example:
    - `Non-Living Skeleton` -> parent `Non-Living Warriors`
    - `Non-Living Zombie` -> parent `Non-Living Warriors`
- `spellRole`
  - tells whether a spell is:
    - `standalone`
    - `parent`
    - `child`
  - example:
    - `Non-Living Warriors` = `parent`
    - `Non-Living Skeleton` = `child`
    - `Assess Character` = `standalone`
- `mode`
  - whether the spell is `active` or `passive`
  - useful because passive spells do not go through cast UI
  - example:
    - `Assess Character` = `active`
    - `Compulsion Guard` = `passive`
- `category`
  - tells what kind of spell it is mechanically
  - useful for action-class mapping and UI field expectations
  - examples:
    - `Necrotic Touch` = `attack`
    - `Boost Physique` = `buff`
    - `Smoldering Shadow` = `aura`
    - `Control Entity` = `control`
    - `Shadow Walk` = `utility`
    - `Assess Character` = `knowledge`
    - `Necromancer's Bless` = `restoration`
    - `Non-Living Skeleton` = `summon`

Short version:
- `parentSpellId`, `spellRole`, `mode`, `category` are useful
- `theme`, `tags`, and the current `globalRules` shape are the parts I would simplify first

If you want, next I can produce a leaner `v1.1` schema.

## My request for Codex:
what does this mean: `        "defaultActionCost": "standard",`

### 754. Assistant

It means:

- if a spell under that `power` does not explicitly define its own `actionCost`
- then the assumed default is `standard`

So it is just a fallback/default value at `power` level, not the final value for every spell.

### 755. Assistant

It means:

- if a spell under that `power` does not explicitly define its own `actionCost`
- then the assumed default is `standard`

So it is just a fallback/default value at `power` level, not the final value for every spell.

## My request for Codex:
what do you say about 1,2,3 ingestion approach? does that make sense or should we be using only one ingestion method, or any other suggestion?

### 768. Assistant

Your `1 -> 2 -> 3` approach makes sense, and I prefer it over one giant ingestion file.

Best version:
1. `Source-normalized JSON`
- close to the text
- captures what the doc says
- records ambiguity, contradictions, missing info

2. `Game-mechanics JSON`
- derived from `1`
- only mechanics/runtime data
- action cost, mana cost, duration, targeting, scaling, effect type, constraints

3. `UI-mechanics JSON`
- derived from `1` and `2`
- only what the player must see/select
- `Power > Spell > Target > Mode > Damage Type`, etc.

My recommendation:
- do not use one file for all three jobs
- do not let `2` and `3` be manually authored from scratch
- make `1` the main human-reviewed source of truth
- derive `2` and `3` from it, plus explicit resolution notes when needed

If I refine it slightly, I would use:
- `0. Raw text`
- `1. Normalized ingestion`
- `1a. Decision log / gap resolution`
- `2. Mechanics-ready`
- `3. UI-ready`

So:
- yes, your layered approach is better
- one single schema is not the right shape for this project

### 816. Assistant

Use `1` as the cleaned rule text, and `1a` as the decision log.

`1` = [power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/power_spell_ingestion_normalized_current.json)

Purpose:
- human-readable normalized source
- one place per power/spell
- records what the spell is supposed to do before coding
- should be reviewed by us before deriving mechanics/UI JSON

Use it like:
- paste/import raw spell text
- normalize into entries: availability, cost, targeting, duration, inputs, rules
- do not include TypeScript class names or UI implementation details

`1a` = [power_spell_ingestion_decisions_current.json](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/power_spell_ingestion_decisions_current.json)

Purpose:
- tracks ambiguities, assumptions, and decisions
- tells us when to ask you for clarification
- prevents hidden assumptions from becoming code

Use it like:
- if source text misses mana cost and that blocks coding, add a gap
- if we choose “Release Control is contextual,” record the decision
- if something is non-blocking like flavor text, do not ask you

Flow:
`raw text -> 1 normalized ingestion -> 1a decisions/gaps -> 2 mechanics JSON -> 3 UI JSON -> code`

- if something is non-blocking like flavor text, do not ask you

Flow:
`raw text -> 1 normalized ingestion -> 1a decisions/gaps -> 2 mechanics JSON -> 3 UI JSON -> code`

"""
6.3. Lessen Darkness (LD) - Active: Activates with the 5th Level of LTBL. Darkness-based and evil creatures in range of LTBL lose one Resistance Level (RL). If they are immune (RL2) to physical/elemental attacks, they become resistant (RL1) to those attacks; if they are resistant (RL1), they lose their resistance (RL0); if they do not have any resistance (RL0), they become vulnerable (RL-1): RL2 -> RL1, RL1 -> RL0, RL0 -> RL-1.

Level 1. Unavailable at this level

Level 2. Unavailable at this level

Level 3. Unavailable at this level

Level 4. Unavailable at this level

Level 5. Activated. Works with LTBL and acquires all other specifics from LTBL.

2. i designed it as if it is a separate spell, because LTBL provides buffs to ally, whilst lessen darkness gives debuffs to enemies. so they have different targets. i could not think a better way to implement that mechanically or in UI, thus I chose this method. as LTBL an aura, would there be a better method for this approach, or its just fine what i had done, and i shold not worry about it?

### 882. Assistant

### 883. Assistant

1. Current implementation is close, but not exact.

- It requires active `Let There Be Light`.
- It costs `0` mana.
- Its effects are source-linked to the LTBL aura, so LTBL source removal should clean it up.
- But it is still exposed as a separate cast-form spell option at level 5: `Power > Spell: Lessen Darkness > Target`.

Relevant code: [lightSupport.ts](/C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/src/powers/lightSupport.ts)

2. Your approach is mechanically fine, but I would refine the UI model.

Best design: keep `Lessen Darkness` as an LTBL child/contextual aura-management effect, not a normal standalone spell. So it would live under active `Let There Be Light`, require no mana/action, select debuff targets, and remain source-linked to LTBL.

Short version: current implementation works, but semantically I’d change it from “separate spell cast” to “LTBL aura management effect.”

## My request for Codex:
1. I did not understand this, explain more and simpler: Its effects are source-linked to the LTBL aura, so LTBL source removal should clean it up. 
2. "But it is still exposed as a separate cast-form spell option at level 5: Power > Spell: Lessen Darkness > Target. " yes, that is how i designed, i explained above why. is that a matter?
3. "Your approach is mechanically fine, but I would refine the UI model.
Best design: keep Lessen Darkness as an LTBL child/contextual aura-management effect, ..." in reference to your best design idea; again, LTBL will have a buff side and a debuff side, if we join both under it, how can we manage targeting? if you select your ally as a target, it will both receive the buff and the debuff. that is not what we want. we want allies to get buffs, and enemies to get debuffs.

### 886. Assistant

1. “Source-linked” means this:

- caster has the main LTBL aura effect
- selected beneficiaries/enemies get copied/linked effects
- those copied/linked effects remember: “I came from this caster’s LTBL aura”
- if the caster’s LTBL aura is removed, all linked effects should be removed too

So if LTBL ends, Lessen Darkness debuffs should also disappear.

2. No, it is not a serious problem.

Your current design works:
`Power > Spell: Lessen Darkness > Target`

It is clear enough and avoids targeting confusion.

3. You’re right about the risk.

If LTBL has both buff and debuff under one UI step, we need separate target groups:
- `Buff targets`
- `Debuff targets`

Otherwise, yes, a selected target could incorrectly get both.

So the better version would be:
- keep `Lessen Darkness` as a separate visible spell/action for now
- internally treat it as LTBL-linked, 0 mana, source-dependent

That gives us:
- clean UI
- no target confusion
- correct aura lifecycle

I would not change it right now unless you want a more complex LTBL management panel later.

- one character already knows an item’s hidden/identified information
- they should be able to share that knowledge with multiple other characters in one UI flow
- instead of only revealing it to one target at a time

- today: item knowledge is very basic
- `B01`: build the real item UI around it, including “share this item’s known info with several selected characters”
